&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:16:&quot;WordPress Planet&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://planet.wordpress.org/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;language&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2:&quot;en&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:47:&quot;WordPress Planet - http://planet.wordpress.org/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;item&quot;;a:50:{i:0;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:82:&quot;WPTavern: Espied: A Free WordPress Portfolio Theme for Designers and Photographers&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=28131&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:206:&quot;http://wptavern.com/espied-a-free-wordpress-portfolio-theme-for-designers-and-photographers?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=espied-a-free-wordpress-portfolio-theme-for-designers-and-photographers&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3633:&quot;&lt;p&gt;If you&amp;#8217;re on the hunt for a new design to showcase your work, WordPress.com&amp;#8217;s beautiful &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.com/themes/espied/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Espied&lt;/a&gt; theme is now available for use on self-hosted sites. This striking minimalist portfolio theme was created with designers, photographers, and artists in mind.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Espied utilizes WordPress.com&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;http://en.support.wordpress.com/portfolios/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;portfolio&lt;/a&gt; feature, which was recently &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/jetpack-rebrands-with-new-logo-adds-custom-post-types-in-3-1-release&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;added to Jetpack&lt;/a&gt;. With this custom content type enabled, users can easily manage and showcase projects with the &lt;code&gt;[portfolio]&lt;/code&gt; shortcode.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/espied.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28131]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/espied.png?resize=880%2C660&quot; alt=&quot;espied&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28133&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Customization options for Espied include support for a 1600 × 320px header image, the ability to set the header text color, and a unique option for setting the thumbnail aspect ratio. Featured image ratio options include landscape (4:3), portrait (3:4), and square (1:1). This setting carries over to archive pages, the portfolio page template, and portfolio shortcodes.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/espied-archive-page.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28131]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/espied-archive-page.png?resize=1025%2C780&quot; alt=&quot;espied-archive-page&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28247&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The theme includes a sidebar that slides out to display navigation and widgets. It is hidden until clicked in order to keep the focus on showcasing your work.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/sidebar.jpg&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28131]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/sidebar.jpg?resize=660%2C336&quot; alt=&quot;sidebar&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28250&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Espied also features a beautiful way to display your social links via a custom menu. Add your social URLs as menu items and the theme will automatically display the right icon, if it&amp;#8217;s available. It currently includes 22 different icons for various social profiles.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/social-links.jpg&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28131]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/social-links.jpg?resize=660%2C305&quot; alt=&quot;social-links&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28249&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Espied showcases images at full width on larger displays so it&amp;#8217;s important to use images that are at least 1272px. Although the theme does include beautiful, readable typography for blogging, the design is probably best-suited for sites that are primarily portfolios or other visual showcases. Check out a &lt;a href=&quot;http://espieddemo.wordpress.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;live demo&lt;/a&gt; on WordPress.com to see the theme in action.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;With the release of Espied, the folks at Automattic are approaching 50 free themes listed on WordPress.org. This portfolio theme is a home run and responds nicely to any screen size. If you want an easy way to showcase your work without having to configure a ton of options, Espied is an excellent choice. &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/themes/espied&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Download&lt;/a&gt; it from the WordPress.org or install it directly via your admin themes panel.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 13 Aug 2014 04:42:00 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:1;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:101:&quot;WPTavern: Theme Checklist Helps Prepare Developers To Submit A Theme To The WordPress Theme Directory&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=28095&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:246:&quot;http://wptavern.com/theme-checklist-helps-prepare-developers-to-submit-a-theme-to-the-wordpress-theme-directory?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=theme-checklist-helps-prepare-developers-to-submit-a-theme-to-the-wordpress-theme-directory&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4406:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a title=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/theme-checklist/&quot; href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/theme-checklist/&quot;&gt;Theme Checklist&lt;/a&gt; is a new plugin by &lt;a title=&quot;http://profiles.wordpress.org/gpriday/&quot; href=&quot;http://profiles.wordpress.org/gpriday/&quot;&gt;Greg Priday&lt;/a&gt; of &lt;a title=&quot;http://siteorigin.com/&quot; href=&quot;http://siteorigin.com/&quot;&gt;SiteOrigin&lt;/a&gt;. The plugin provides a checklist of items to go through before submitting a theme to the WordPress theme directory. Once activated, you&amp;#8217;ll find the checklist under &lt;strong&gt;Tools &amp;gt; Theme Checklist.&lt;/strong&gt; Theme developers check off each item that successfully passes a test. Themes need to pass all tests before they can be accepted into the &lt;a title=&quot;http://wordpress.org/themes/&quot; href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/themes/&quot;&gt;WordPress theme directory&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/ThemeChecklist.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28095]&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-28195&quot; src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/ThemeChecklist.png?resize=790%2C461&quot; alt=&quot;Check List Of Items To Go Through&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Check List Of Items To Go Through
&lt;p&gt;If a test doesn&amp;#8217;t pass, you can select the X and a small text area appears allowing you to write and save notes to that item. There are a total of 31 different tests ranging from Code Quality to Security. Each item has a link that takes users to a page on &lt;a title=&quot;http://themechecklist.org/&quot; href=&quot;http://themechecklist.org/&quot;&gt;Themechecklist.org&lt;/a&gt; with more information. Theme Checklist also contains the ability to import or export tests enabling users to collaborate on testing themes in different environments.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I used Theme Checklist to review the WP Tavern theme and it passed with flying colors.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/ThemeChecklistResults.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28095]&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-28199&quot; src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/ThemeChecklistResults.png?resize=844%2C186&quot; alt=&quot;Ravel Passes Tests With Flying Colors&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;WP Tavern Theme Passes With Flying Colors
&lt;h2&gt;Theme Checklist Is An Alternative Learning Experience&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/ThemeCheckListFeaturedImage.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28095]&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-28218&quot; src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/ThemeCheckListFeaturedImage.png?resize=638%2C298&quot; alt=&quot;Theme Check List Featured Image&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;photo credit: &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.flickr.com/photos/justin_case/6089119290/&quot;&gt;Dr Case&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; &lt;a href=&quot;http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc/2.0/&quot;&gt;cc&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Although the plugin is not an exact match, Priday will do his best to keep the checklist in line with the official &lt;a title=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/docs/theme-developer-handbook/part-four-releasing-your-theme/theme-review-guidelines/&quot; href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/docs/theme-developer-handbook/part-four-releasing-your-theme/theme-review-guidelines/&quot;&gt;WordPress.org Theme Review Guidelines&lt;/a&gt;.  &amp;#8220;My goal is to make a kind of Dummies Guide to The Theme Review Guidelines&amp;#8221; Priday said. &amp;#8220;I’ve generally found that the theme review guidelines are really difficult for new theme developers to understand. I’ve tried to make something that makes all the requirements easier to understand.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Theme Checklist is not meant to be a replacement for the &lt;a title=&quot;https://wordpress.org/plugins/theme-check/&quot; href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/plugins/theme-check/&quot;&gt;Theme Check&lt;/a&gt; plugin. Instead, it&amp;#8217;s a collection of the most common snag points witnessed by Priday in the theme review queue. According to Priday, the queue has a five-week backlog. He hopes Theme Checklist helps decrease the queue and gets more theme developers to pass the initial review.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I understand why the theme review guidelines need to be thorough and specific. It&amp;#8217;s the WordPress.org theme directory and they help create a consistent user experience. Plugins like Theme Checklist provide an alternative learning experience to accomplish the same goal. However, it has to remain on par with the official guidelines or else it could end up doing more harm than good.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Theme developers, is this a tool you see yourself using? What other tools do you use to increase the likelihood of passing a review on the first try?&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 12 Aug 2014 22:45:08 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:2;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:89:&quot;WPTavern: Right Meow Plugin Puts The Super Troopers Cat Game Into Your WordPress Comments&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=28201&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:222:&quot;http://wptavern.com/right-meow-plugin-puts-the-super-troopers-cat-game-into-your-wordpress-comments?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=right-meow-plugin-puts-the-super-troopers-cat-game-into-your-wordpress-comments&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1976:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Broken Lizard&amp;#8217;s 2001 comedy &amp;#8220;&lt;a href=&quot;http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0247745/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Super Troopers&lt;/a&gt;&amp;#8221; introduced millions of viewers to the &amp;#8220;cat game.&amp;#8221; In the scene, a highway patrolman pulls Jim Gaffigan over and then tries to insert the word &amp;#8220;meow&amp;#8221; casually into the conversation as many times as possible. You remember that scene, right? If not, check it out here:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;embed-youtube&quot;&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Am I Saying Meow?!&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Now, you can also have subliminal meow fun with &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/right-meow/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Right Meow&lt;/a&gt;, a WordPress plugin that changes your comments section so that the word &amp;#8220;now&amp;#8221; automatically becomes &amp;#8220;meow,&amp;#8221; as shown below:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/meow.jpg&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28201]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/meow.jpg?resize=766%2C461&quot; alt=&quot;meow&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28205&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The plugin was created by &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.thomasleen.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Thomas Leen&lt;/a&gt; and is his first submission on WordPress.org. It&amp;#8217;s also available on &lt;a href=&quot;https://github.com/tleen/wp-right-meow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;GitHub&lt;/a&gt;, should you want to suggest any changes. After testing it, I can confirm that it works as advertised to transform all instances of &amp;#8220;now&amp;#8221; to &amp;#8220;meow&amp;#8221; in the comments.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This may not be the most productive tool in the shed but it definitely adds a dash of frivolity and fun to your site by automatically trolling commenters with meows on your behalf. Please note that de-activating the plugin will return all your &amp;#8220;meows&amp;#8221; back to &amp;#8220;nows.&amp;#8221; If you want your comments to have a little more entertainment value, I recommend you &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/right-meow/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;download&lt;/a&gt; this plugin right meow.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 12 Aug 2014 22:20:08 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:3;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:69:&quot;Alex King: The Race to the Bottom Benefits Platforms (not Developers)&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://alexking.org/?p=20713&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:60:&quot;http://alexking.org/blog/2014/08/12/race-to-bottom-platforms&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3773:&quot;&lt;p&gt;There&amp;#8217;s been a ton of recent conversation in the iOS world about the inability for most indie developers to create sustainable businesses through the iOS app store. In particular, these devs are talking about apps that require larger development efforts &amp;#8211; they want to charge more than &amp;#8220;impulse purchase&amp;#8221; prices for these, and thus want trials, upgrade pricing, etc. to support that model. They want things to work they way they always have &amp;#8211; I don&amp;#8217;t blame them.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I think it&amp;#8217;s worth considering who wins in this &amp;#8220;race to the bottom&amp;#8221;. In general, more stuff for free benefits consumers, which in turn benefits the platform.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;But wait!&amp;#8221; the developers cry. &amp;#8220;When the platform doesn&amp;#8217;t support building more sophisticated apps, the consumers ultimately lose!&amp;#8221; I know this argument, I&amp;#8217;ve made it myself regarding the WordPress ecosystem. I was wrong.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Consumers have been well trained that they can expect incredible value for free. Sure, they may trade off their privacy and be subjected to ads, but they aren&amp;#8217;t asked to fork over their cash directly.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;VC-backed companies often contribute to the problem as well. As they clamor for users to their platforms, they give everything away &amp;#8211; it&amp;#8217;s so easy to flip the switch in the future and start the money pouring in. Or if that doesn&amp;#8217;t work, they fold up shop and call it a day. Oops!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;More complex apps &lt;em&gt;will get made&lt;/em&gt;. They just won&amp;#8217;t be built using the model that indie developers are used to.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;There will be apps supported by alternative revenue streams. Some might have ads or sponsorships, some might mine and sell the data they produce, some (like Evernote and Dropbox) will be a gateway to a commercial service. People will figure out ways to get money out of a large enough user base, and apps will get built.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I&amp;#8217;ve seen this happen in the WordPress ecosystem already. It&amp;#8217;s a different beast because it&amp;#8217;s an Open Source community, but it&amp;#8217;s still an interesting parallel.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Basically this happened:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ol&gt;
&lt;li&gt;A bunch of folks built stuff and released it all for free to a small community, largely consisting of fellow developers and tinkerers&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;A whole bunch more folks started using the platform and the community grew &amp;#8211; it wasn&amp;#8217;t just developers anymore, it was end users with expectations of support, etc.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Devs wanted to start monetizing the products they were providing&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;The platform didn&amp;#8217;t provide the tools to make money in the way that the devs wanted -instead it invested in tools to promote free products&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Eventually a variety of patterns arose to monetize both commercial and &amp;#8220;free&amp;#8221; products (subscription clubs with access to a bunch of different plugins/themes, free products with commercial add-ons, sponsorships and ads, products that were created to support hosting services, etc.)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ol&gt;
&lt;p&gt;It&amp;#8217;s not the  &lt;img src=&quot;http://alexking.org/wp-content/themes/alexking.org-v3/smilies/ak_scare1.gif&quot; alt=&quot;:scare:&quot; class=&quot;wp-smiley&quot; /&gt;  pure  &lt;img src=&quot;http://alexking.org/wp-content/themes/alexking.org-v3/smilies/ak_scare2.gif&quot; alt=&quot;:/scare:&quot; class=&quot;wp-smiley&quot; /&gt;  and direct approach of charging directly for the software, but it&amp;#8217;s still developers writing code and making money.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The same thing is happening for iOS. There is money to be made. The platform and consumers are winning.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Adapt or die&amp;#8221; is our mantra for those business who are threatened by technology. We have little sympathy for newspapers, the music industry, etc. Perhaps it&amp;#8217;s time to include software companies in that list.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 12 Aug 2014 21:53:56 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4:&quot;Alex&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:4;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:110:&quot;WPTavern: Sprout Apps to Launch a Suite of WordPress-Powered Apps Targeted at Freelancers and Small Businesses&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=28141&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:264:&quot;http://wptavern.com/sprout-apps-to-launch-a-suite-of-wordpress-powered-apps-targeted-at-freelancers-and-small-businesses?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=sprout-apps-to-launch-a-suite-of-wordpress-powered-apps-targeted-at-freelancers-and-small-businesses&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:6601:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/sprout-apps.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28141]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/sprout-apps.png?resize=1025%2C464&quot; alt=&quot;sprout-apps&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28152&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://sproutapps.co/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Sprout Apps&lt;/a&gt; will soon be launching a suite of business apps targeted at WordPress freelancers and small businesses. WordPress developer &lt;a href=&quot;http://dancameron.org/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Daniel Cameron&lt;/a&gt; is behind the project, which is centered around creating plugins that help business owners work more efficiently with WordPress. Sprout Apps aims to bring tasks like invoicing, estimates, and client tracking into the admin.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Cameron is the creator of &lt;a href=&quot;http://smartecart.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Smart eCart&lt;/a&gt;, a popular solution for daily deals, crowdfunding and social commerce. For five years he has supported and maintained the plugin, which was originally created for a client project. With the desire to venture out and create something new, Cameron has soft-launched Sprout Apps, starting with &lt;a href=&quot;https://sproutapps.co/sprout-invoices/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Sprout Invoices&lt;/a&gt;, now available for purchase.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/sprout-apps-invoices.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28141]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/sprout-apps-invoices.png?resize=500%2C387&quot; alt=&quot;sprout-apps-invoices&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-large wp-image-28154&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Sprout Invoicing is an idea that Cameron had cooked up year ago but was hesitant about, due to the fact that other plugin developers had explored it without much success.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;I went back to my original idea that I had years ago, which was a new invoicing app that solved all the problems I’ve had with Freshbooks and Harvest,&amp;#8221; he said. &amp;#8220;I knew there were already plugins out there which made me reluctant to pursue it further, regardless if their approach was wrong in my opinion.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Sprout Invoicing Aims to Help Streamline and Brand All Client Communications&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In order to sell his product, Cameron will have to convince business owners of the value in using a WordPress-powered invoicing system instead of the many standalone services. He&amp;#8217;s counting on customers&amp;#8217; desire to &lt;a href=&quot;https://sproutapps.co/news/what-sprout-invoices-solves-for-freelancers-and-wordpress-sites/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;streamline all aspects of their businesses&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Those other standalone services are silo’d, expensive, limiting and offer limited customization for brand integrity,&amp;#8221; Cameron contends. &amp;#8220;I want to streamline the estimate and invoicing process. Integrating it within the site that already has the estimate request (contact form) helps tremendously.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In addition to fully automating estimating and invoicing, the app is designed to help business owners overcome the branding limitations of popular invoicing services, which generally only let you upload a logo to a subdomain. The freedom to fully brand all client communications is a big win for small businesses.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Sprout Invoice notification emails are sent from your server and your from address,&amp;#8221; Cameron said. &amp;#8220;No more http://yoursite.harvestbooks.com with a &amp;#8216;Powered by A Service I Pay For&amp;#8217;.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The invoicing app is built with business owner&amp;#8217;s needs in mind. It&amp;#8217;s packed full of dashboards and charts, summaries, and dynamic reporting that can be easily sorted and filtered in the WordPress admin.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/sprout-invoicing-charts.gif&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28141]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/sprout-invoicing-charts.gif?resize=606%2C342&quot; alt=&quot;sprout-invoicing-charts&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28159&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Under the hood, Sprout Invoices is a WordPress plugin that uses custom post types, post meta and taxonomies for its data structure. &amp;#8220;There are no additional tables created. The entire code base adheres to WordPress coding practices,&amp;#8221; Cameron told the Tavern. &amp;#8220;There&amp;#8217;s hundreds of hooks and filters in SI, I want the entire app to be customizable and I anticipate it’s users to want more control than traditional WP users.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The apps he &lt;a href=&quot;https://sproutapps.co/coming-soon/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;plans to build&lt;/a&gt; are actually WordPress plugins, though he felt that apps was a more applicable term. &amp;#8220;I didn’t want to go with &amp;#8216;Sprout plugins,&amp;#8217; for example, because I do have ideas that aren&amp;#8217;t plugins and I didn&amp;#8217;t want to box myself in,&amp;#8221; he said. &amp;#8220;I also think &amp;#8216;Apps&amp;#8217; is a better term for these larger premium plugins since they offer more than a traditional plugin that might filter post content.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Sprout&amp;#8217;s next app will be a CRM, followed by a team-based app. Cameron is also considering a PM app and a time tracker, depending on how sales go with the invoicing app. &lt;a href=&quot;https://sproutapps.co/sprout-invoices/purchase/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Pricing&lt;/a&gt; for Sprouts Invoicing is similar to that of popular invoicing services, with both monthly and yearly subscription rates at $5 and $9 respectively. Subscribers will receive updates, support and &lt;a href=&quot;https://sproutapps.co/marketplace/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;add-on&lt;/a&gt; discounts. Cameron also plans to launch a free version of the invoicing app later this year.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Sprout Apps is built on the bold premise that your WordPress site can be more than just the marketing face of your business. It can also power the daily tasks of estimating work, billing clients, and charting progress. Cameron is aiming to provide all the business essentials with the added benefit of brand independence, a streamlined workflow, and total control. He&amp;#8217;s got a big vision to create a superior suite of apps that will support the many freelancers and small businesses that make up a large segment of the WordPress ecosystem.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://sproutapps.co/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Sprout Apps&lt;/a&gt; is currently in pre-launch mode and will officially launch at &lt;a href=&quot;http://2014.la.wordcamp.org/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WordCamp LA&lt;/a&gt; in early September. A &lt;a href=&quot;https://sproutapps.co/demos/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;live demo&lt;/a&gt; of the app is available to preview and pre-launch subscribers will receive a discount at purchase.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 12 Aug 2014 20:54:38 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:5;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:40:&quot;WPTavern: WP Site Care Acquires Audit WP&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=28140&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:124:&quot;http://wptavern.com/wp-site-care-acquires-audit-wp?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=wp-site-care-acquires-audit-wp&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1996:&quot;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/MergeFeaturedImage.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28140]&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-28143&quot; src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/MergeFeaturedImage.png?resize=678%2C252&quot; alt=&quot;Merge Featured Image&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;photo credit: &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.flickr.com/photos/rutlo/3743291132/&quot;&gt;rutlo&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; &lt;a href=&quot;http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/2.0/&quot;&gt;cc&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a title=&quot;http://auditwp.com/&quot; href=&quot;http://auditwp.com/&quot;&gt;Audit WP&lt;/a&gt; has been acquired by &lt;a title=&quot;http://www.wpsitecare.com&quot; href=&quot;http://www.wpsitecare.com&quot;&gt;WP Site Care&lt;/a&gt;. According to &lt;a title=&quot;http://www.wpsitecare.com/rob-neu-auditwp-join-wp-site-care/&quot; href=&quot;http://www.wpsitecare.com/rob-neu-auditwp-join-wp-site-care/&quot;&gt;the announcement&lt;/a&gt;, Audit WP will operate under WP Site Care while continuing to offer specialized SEO services. Rob Neu, who owned and operated Audit WP, will become WP Site Care&amp;#8217;s Director of Digital Strategy.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Rob will oversee product development as well as making sure that our brand, services, and content align with our ultimate goal of providing top-tier WordPress support, and making WordPress an asset for our clients and people who are new to the platform.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Neu hints that new SEO training packages are being worked on and a new plugin is being developed that will make it easier for WP Site Care customers to receive support from the WordPress dashboard.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Neu cites his passion for wanting to help businesses and individuals as one of the primary reasons for merging with WP Site Care. &amp;#8220;At my core, the thing I like the most about everything that I do is that I’m able help people,&amp;#8221; Neu said. &amp;#8220;I want to help people improve their businesses, make more money, and be more successful.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;By joining WP Site Care, a business dedicated to helping people solve WordPress problems, he&amp;#8217;s in a great position to do just that.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 12 Aug 2014 18:26:30 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:6;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:22:&quot;Matt: The Great Filter&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:21:&quot;http://ma.tt/?p=43964&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:36:&quot;http://ma.tt/2014/08/thegreatfilter/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:423:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;embed-youtube&quot;&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This is about the Great Filter. (No, not &lt;a href=&quot;http://akismet.com/&quot;&gt;Akismet&lt;/a&gt;.) It&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.overcomingbias.com/2014/07/adam-ford-i-on-great-filter.html&quot;&gt;Adam Ford and Robert Hanson&lt;/a&gt; on existential risks to humanity, a continuation of the Fermi Paradox discussion I &lt;a href=&quot;http://ma.tt/2014/07/the-fermi-paradox/&quot;&gt;posted about the other day&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 12 Aug 2014 16:39:00 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:14:&quot;Matt Mullenweg&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:7;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:78:&quot;Post Status: Audit WP to become part of WP Site Care with acquihire of Rob Neu&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:30:&quot;http://www.poststat.us/?p=7078&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:108:&quot;http://www.poststat.us/wp-site-care-rob-neu/?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=wp-site-care-rob-neu&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3669:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;aligncenter size-large wp-image-7081&quot; src=&quot;http://www.poststat.us/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/wp-site-care-752x341.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;wp-site-care&quot; width=&quot;627&quot; height=&quot;284&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Audit WP had a short, but interesting life span. Started by &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/rob_neu&quot;&gt;Rob Neu&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://jacobking.com&quot;&gt;Jacob King&lt;/a&gt;, the site launched in February, and &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.wpsitecare.com/rob-neu-auditwp-join-wp-site-care/&quot;&gt;today it&amp;#8217;s been acquired by WP Site Care&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;They made an early splash after their launch when Jacob &lt;a href=&quot;http://auditwp.com/wp-engine-seo-failboat/&quot;&gt;wrote a provocative post&lt;/a&gt; about WP Engine&amp;#8217;s SEO policies. Aside from that, they set out to productize technical SEO and general website strategy.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Their product was fairly successful, but they learned a valuable lesson; they were limiting their consulting opportunities for larger contracts by productizing &amp;#8212; and therefore bracketing themselves at a relatively low price &amp;#8212; their entry level services. That said, the product was quite good, and will now be part of WP Site Care&amp;#8217;s offering in the form of a la carte SEO consulting, reports, and tools.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I had a call with Rob and Jacob a couple of months ago to demo their product, and because I needed real help from them. I&amp;#8217;d been getting clobbered by Google, and they helped me identify some of the reasons why and set about a plan to fix it. I&amp;#8217;m still working on it, and was very pleased with what they offered.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;aligncenter size-large wp-image-7079&quot; src=&quot;http://www.poststat.us/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/audit-wp-overview-752x488.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;audit-wp-overview&quot; width=&quot;627&quot; height=&quot;406&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This and other tools were quite nice, and the value I got from a short call and report were pretty enormous. I think this will be a compelling product for WP Site Care&amp;#8217;s services, and it will fit in well with their other offerings.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you know Rob Neu and WP Site Care&amp;#8217;s owner, Ryan Sullivan, then you already know they are friends. Rob joining WP Site Care doesn&amp;#8217;t come as a shock, and seems to make sense all around. The two are already working on a separate side project together, called &lt;a href=&quot;http://flagshipwp.com/&quot;&gt;Flagship&lt;/a&gt;, a theme company. Additionally, WP Site Care was a sponsor and often attendee on WP Bacon, Rob&amp;#8217;s old podcast that also unfortunately bit the dust.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Rob and Ryan&amp;#8217;s partnership for Flagship will remain separate, and Rob will be the Director of Digital Strategy for WP Site Care, now a team of five full time employees. Rob is a technical guy, and in addition to running strategy and marketing for WP Site Care, he&amp;#8217;ll be working on refining some of their product offerings as well.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;What is WP Site Care anyway?&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I talked about WP Site Care and other &lt;a title=&quot;The rise of WordPress maintenance services&quot; href=&quot;http://www.poststat.us/rise-wordpress-maintenance-services/&quot;&gt;WordPress maintenance services&lt;/a&gt; earlier this year. Essentially it&amp;#8217;s a combination of monthly maintenance and support, and a la carte services. It&amp;#8217;s been a wildly successful and growing niche in the WordPress market, and there seem to be new companies popping up every day.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;While I don&amp;#8217;t know the degree of professionalism and expertise all of them have, I know that at least a few are very good at what they do. &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.wpsitecare.com&quot;&gt;WP Site Care&lt;/a&gt; adding Rob and the variety of tools he brings to the table is a smart move for them to help set themselves apart in what is quickly becoming a crowded market.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 12 Aug 2014 15:59:47 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:15:&quot;Brian Krogsgard&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:8;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:85:&quot;WPTavern: Add Reddit Style Commenting to WordPress With the Comment Popularity Plugin&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=28045&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:214:&quot;http://wptavern.com/add-reddit-style-commenting-to-wordpress-with-the-comment-popularity-plugin?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=add-reddit-style-commenting-to-wordpress-with-the-comment-popularity-plugin&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:5010:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/comments.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28045]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/comments.png?resize=984%2C455&quot; alt=&quot;comments&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28128&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Comments are an important aspect of your content and can serve as a vehicle for building community. WordPress site admins put in a hefty amount of work moderating comments and combating spam, just to &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/why-comments-still-matter&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;keep the conversation going&lt;/a&gt; with comments open. With all that work invested, admins are looking for new ways to make comment interaction more valuable to those who are participating.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress.com recently&lt;a href=&quot;http://en.blog.wordpress.com/2014/08/07/introducing-comment-likes/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt; added comment likes&lt;/a&gt; to the delight of its users. Self-hosted WordPress site admins are hopeful that comment likes will find their way into Jetpack as well. If you&amp;#8217;re interested in doing something more with comments, there are many plugins that help to promote interaction on your site.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/comment-popularity/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Comment Popularity&lt;/a&gt; is a new one that caught my eye. The plugin, created by &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/paul_wp&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Paul de Wouters&lt;/a&gt; and his colleagues at &lt;a href=&quot;http://hmn.md/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Human Made&lt;/a&gt;, adds Reddit style commenting to WordPress. Registered site members can vote comments up or down to increase or decrease comment visibility.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/comment-popularity.jpg&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28045]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/comment-popularity.jpg?resize=785%2C613&quot; alt=&quot;comment-popularity&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28093&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;When the plugin is active, comments are sorted by weight (number of votes) in a descending order. Site members receive karma each time one of their comments is upvoted. Administrators have the option to attribute more weight to &amp;#8220;expert&amp;#8221; commenters by adding an expert label and additional points on user profiles.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/user-profile-comment-popularity-settings.jpg&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28045]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/user-profile-comment-popularity-settings.jpg?resize=503%2C234&quot; alt=&quot;user-profile-comment-popularity-settings&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28102&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;There&amp;#8217;s also an option in the discussion panel for setting a default expert karma.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;De Wouters and the folks at Human Made plan to support and maintain the plugin via the forums on WordPress.org. It was originally created for their client, CFO Publishing, who will be listed as a contributor on the next release.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&amp;#8220;I have a few ideas for integration with other plugins such as Stream, and our SaaS product WP Remote,&amp;#8221;&lt;/strong&gt; de Wouters said. I asked if he plans to add a UI for showing users their aggregate upvotes/ranks, and he confirmed that this is a possibility. &amp;#8220;We&amp;#8217;re already storing users voting activity, so it makes sense to offer an admin view for it,&amp;#8221; he said. &amp;#8220;Maybe a dashboard widget. Also, this is the kind of data we&amp;#8217;d send to WP Remote or Stream.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The plugin is currently restricted to registered users, as it doesn&amp;#8217;t make much sense to leave it open for anonymous users to vote. &amp;#8220;I do however plan to develop a drop in class that will allow users to authenticate themselves via social networks, which will reduce friction and still provide a way to identify a user with relative reliabilty,&amp;#8221; de Wouters commented regarding future development plans. Although he wants to keep it simple and focused on one particular functionality, he is open to suggestions and contributions via the plugin&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;https://github.com/humanmade/comment-popularity&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;GitHub repository&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Comment Popularity gives registered users a way to weigh in on discussions without having to comment. Consequently, there is a greater incentive for readers to register for your site. It gives everyone a chance to influence the conversation. As users attribute value to comments they like, the best comments will float to the top. This saves readers from having to scroll through all the mediocre comments in order to find the highest quality responses.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you&amp;#8217;re looking for a new way to encourage interaction in your comments, the Comment Popularity plugin is simple and intuitive to use. It should work automatically with most standard comment forms. &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/comment-popularity/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Download&lt;/a&gt; the plugin for free from WordPress.org and watch the GitHub repository for updates in development.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 12 Aug 2014 00:14:59 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:12;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:77:&quot;WPTavern: Interview With Siobhan McKeown On The Future Of The WordPress Codex&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=28089&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:198:&quot;http://wptavern.com/interview-with-siobhan-mckeown-on-the-future-of-the-wordpress-codex?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=interview-with-siobhan-mckeown-on-the-future-of-the-wordpress-codex&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:6798:&quot;&lt;p&gt;If you use WordPress, chances are that you&amp;#8217;ve run into the &lt;a title=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/&quot; href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/&quot;&gt;WordPress Codex&lt;/a&gt;. The Codex is a community maintained collection of documentation, hooks, filters, best practices, and other information related to WordPress. With various &lt;a title=&quot;http://make.wordpress.org/docs/handbook/projects/handbooks/&quot; href=&quot;http://make.wordpress.org/docs/handbook/projects/handbooks/&quot;&gt;handbook projects&lt;/a&gt; underway, I&amp;#8217;ve been wondering what the future of the Codex is. To find out, I got in touch with &lt;a title=&quot;http://siobhanmckeown.com/&quot; href=&quot;http://siobhanmckeown.com/&quot;&gt;Siobhan McKeown&lt;/a&gt;, who is a member of the &lt;a title=&quot;http://make.wordpress.org/docs/&quot; href=&quot;http://make.wordpress.org/docs/&quot;&gt;documentation team&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Interview With Siobhan McKeown&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Is the &lt;a title=&quot;http://make.wordpress.org/docs/2013/06/19/docs-sprint-results-and-roadmap/&quot; href=&quot;http://make.wordpress.org/docs/2013/06/19/docs-sprint-results-and-roadmap/&quot;&gt;roadmap outlined here&lt;/a&gt; still accurate and is it being followed? Is it still on time?&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The roadmap is still fairly accurate but it’s not on time. The number of contributors to docs is quite small and we’ve faced challenges around getting development work done and finding people to write. That said, the people who are involved are very dedicated and we’re slowly chipping away at things. We have made big strides forward, particularly in the area of inline docs (thanks &lt;a title=&quot;http://profiles.wordpress.org/drewapicture&quot; href=&quot;http://profiles.wordpress.org/drewapicture&quot;&gt;Drew Jaynes&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a title=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/kpdesign&quot; href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/kpdesign&quot;&gt;Kim Parsell&lt;/a&gt;) and in building &lt;a title=&quot;https://developer.wordpress.org/reference/&quot; href=&quot;https://developer.wordpress.org/reference/&quot;&gt;developer.wordpress.org&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Ultimately, is the future of the Codex for it to disappear in favor of all the other documentation resources outlined in the roadmap?&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I would like for that to happen, but the decision doesn’t ultimately lie with me and it’s a discussion that we’ll have to return to once new documentation is in place.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Many free software projects in the early stages of their life use a wiki for their documentation. Over time, this can become out-of-date and inaccurate. As a project grows, it often out-grows a wiki, requiring more targeted documentation for both users and developers. &lt;a href=&quot;https://support.mozilla.org/en-US/products/firefox&quot;&gt;Firefox&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://guides.rubyonrails.org/getting_started.html&quot;&gt;Ruby on Rails&lt;/a&gt; are good examples of FOSS projects that provide the types of targeted documentation that WordPress should be providing. I would hope that we can eventually get there ourselves, and keep the Codex as a historical archive.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/MozillaFireFoxTargetedSupport.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28089]&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-28100&quot; src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/MozillaFireFoxTargetedSupport.png?resize=966%2C690&quot; alt=&quot;Mozilla FireFox Targeted Documentation&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Mozilla FireFox Targeted Documentation
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Is it a waste of effort and energy for folks to continue to edit and update the Codex?&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;No. For two reasons: First of all, while all of the docs work is going on, we need to ensure that the Codex stays up-to-date and accurate. It remains WordPress’ primary source of documentation and will be for some time, so contributions are still valuable there. When a new version of WordPress is released, the docs team usually does a sprint to get the Codex up-to-date.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Secondly, the main problem with the Codex is its navigation and structure. There’s a lot of good content in there mixed with a lot of out-of-date content. As we create new resources, we look at the content in the Codex and migrate good-quality content. If you fix a page in the Codex, then it’s likely that will end up somewhere in a new documentation resource.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;How can folks get involved with helping the roadmap move along?&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We particularly need help in two areas:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ol&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Someone to help with ongoing development of &lt;a title=&quot;http://wptavern.com/help-contribute-to-the-official-wordpress-developer-resource-by-testing-code-references&quot; href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/help-contribute-to-the-official-wordpress-developer-resource-by-testing-code-references&quot;&gt;WP-Parser&lt;/a&gt; (the parser used to generate the Code Reference). A lot of things are on hold until we get someone helping there.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Writing the &lt;a title=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/docs/theme-developer-handbook/&quot; href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/docs/theme-developer-handbook/&quot;&gt;theme&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a title=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/docs/plugin-developer-handbook/&quot; href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/docs/plugin-developer-handbook/&quot;&gt;plugin developer&lt;/a&gt; handbooks. These have been around for a long time and we really want to get them finished off so that we can move on to focusing on user support.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ol&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;To Some, Google Is The WordPress Codex&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;It may be the largest collection of WordPress documentation but I bet it doesn&amp;#8217;t compare to the amount of WordPress content published on sites across the web. The paradox of publishing content on the Codex for the benefit of everyone versus a personal site for the benefit of a small audience has existed since it was created.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I think it would be awesome if content from sites like &lt;a title=&quot;http://justintadlock.com/&quot; href=&quot;http://justintadlock.com/&quot;&gt;Justin Tadlock&lt;/a&gt; found a home on the Codex but perhaps we don&amp;#8217;t need one at all. Maybe all we need is Google. When I asked the Tavern&amp;#8217;s Twitter followers what &lt;a title=&quot;http://wptavern.com/7-aspects-of-wordpress-i-take-for-granted&quot; href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/7-aspects-of-wordpress-i-take-for-granted&quot;&gt;aspect of WordPress do they take for granted&lt;/a&gt;, Jared Novack submitted the following answer:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot; width=&quot;550&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/wptavern&quot;&gt;@wptavern&lt;/a&gt; You can type anything into google followed by &quot;WordPress&quot; and someone has already asked (and answered) it&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; Jared Novack (@jaredNova) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/jaredNova/statuses/494322903739936768&quot;&gt;July 30, 2014&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If the Codex ever goes offline, it will be a sad day. However, if it&amp;#8217;s replaced with easy to navigate, skill level targeted documentation, with a solid code reference, I think a lot of users and developers will be happy with its replacement. Has the Codex saved your bacon once or twice? Let us know in the comments.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Mon, 11 Aug 2014 22:20:27 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:13;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:57:&quot;WPTavern: WPWeekly Episode 157 – Jeffro Tells His Story&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:44:&quot;http://wptavern.com?p=28075&amp;preview_id=28075&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:150:&quot;http://wptavern.com/wpweekly-episode-157-jeffro-tells-his-story?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=wpweekly-episode-157-jeffro-tells-his-story&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2274:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The past 156 episodes of WordPress Weekly are filled with stories of people who are doing exciting things with WordPress. For this episode, I decided to try something a little different. I handed the show over to &lt;a href=&quot;http://marcuscouch.com/&quot; title=&quot;http://marcuscouch.com/&quot;&gt;Marcus Couch&lt;/a&gt;, who interviewed me. In the show, I describe how I became interested in computers and the events that lead me to where I am today. It&amp;#8217;s a lengthy episode but one I hope you enjoy.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;A reminder that beginning this week, WordPress Weekly will be recorded live on &lt;strong&gt;Wednesdays at 9:30 PM Eastern&lt;/strong&gt;. The change better accommodates my schedule and the new day and time is also more compatible with guests.&lt;/p&gt;
