&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Listen To Episode #157:&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Mon, 11 Aug 2014 20:05:12 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:14;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:67:&quot;WPTavern: Underscores WordPress Starter Theme Adds Support for Sass&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=28061&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:178:&quot;http://wptavern.com/underscores-wordpress-starter-theme-adds-support-for-sass?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=underscores-wordpress-starter-theme-adds-support-for-sass&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3186:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://underscores.me/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Underscores&lt;/a&gt; community project contributors &lt;a href=&quot;http://themeshaper.com/2014/08/11/sass-comes-to-_s/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;announced&lt;/a&gt; today that the theme now includes support for &lt;a href=&quot;http://sass-lang.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Sass&lt;/a&gt;. The popular WordPress starter theme is an open source project maintained by Automattic, and many of its users requested Sass support, according to contributor Tammie Lister. &amp;#8220;The community firstly asked for Sass. As Sass is in core, this makes sense. It was already part of most themers&amp;#8217; workflow.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you visit &lt;a href=&quot;http://underscores.me/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Underscores.me&lt;/a&gt; and click on &amp;#8220;Advanced Options&amp;#8221;, you&amp;#8217;ll now find that you can check a box to add Sass support:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/add-sass.jpg&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28061]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/add-sass.jpg?resize=968%2C355&quot; alt=&quot;add-sass&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28068&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Lister emphasized in the announcement that support for Sass is included in a way that gives developers the freedom to use it as they please:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Not everyone compiles or uses Sass the same, so _s shouldn&amp;#8217;t force anyone to follow one path or another. In this sense, the Sass provided takes a pure approach, not requiring Compass or any other scripts.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Sass support came about from a combination of numerous pull requests and forks of the project on GitHub. However, the project&amp;#8217;s contributors do not wish to limit everyone to Sass and are open to other CSS preprocessors. &lt;strong&gt;&amp;#8220;I&amp;#8217;d still love to see a fork of Less for _s. We&amp;#8217;re keen it opens up the way to other preprocessors,&amp;#8221;&lt;/strong&gt; Lister told the Tavern regarding the Sass support announced today.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Earlier this year, &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/wordpress-com-formally-opens-its-marketplace-to-theme-developers&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WordPress.com formally opened up its marketplace to theme developers&lt;/a&gt;. Theme submission &lt;a href=&quot;http://developer.wordpress.com/themes/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;guidelines&lt;/a&gt; are fairly strict and developers are encouraged to use the _s theme for a head start. While many theme authors appreciate the ability to save time with mixins and variables, using a preprocessor is not required for submitting to WordPress.com.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Every WordPress themer has a unique workflow that may or may not involve a preprocessor, and the Underscores project contributors plan to respect that. &lt;strong&gt;&amp;#8220;_s doesn&amp;#8217;t tell you how to do things, it gives you a start. Anything we add to it should also do that,&amp;#8221;&lt;/strong&gt; Lister said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The addition of Sass support marks another turning point for the project, as Lister notes that the &lt;a href=&quot;https://github.com/Automattic/_s&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;GitHub repository&lt;/a&gt; will now be used solely for development. If you want to use Underscores in a project, the team encourages you to download it directly from &lt;a href=&quot;http://underscores.me/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Underscores.me&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Mon, 11 Aug 2014 19:00:58 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:15;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:93:&quot;Post Status: Week in review: theme shops, hub and spoke, you can’t afford me, and much more&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:30:&quot;http://www.poststat.us/?p=7070&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:168:&quot;http://www.poststat.us/week-review-theme-shops-hub-spoke-cant-afford-much/?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=week-review-theme-shops-hub-spoke-cant-afford-much&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:10330:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;aligncenter size-large wp-image-6769&quot; src=&quot;http://www.poststat.us/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/week-in-review1-752x300.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;week-in-review&quot; width=&quot;627&quot; height=&quot;250&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Welcome to the seventh “&lt;a href=&quot;http://www.poststat.us/category/week-in-review/&quot;&gt;Week in Review&lt;/a&gt;” on Post Status, where I hope to offer up some of the things you may have missed in the last week or so. A whole bunch of good stuff to read from the last week, so let&amp;#8217;s get to it:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Theme shops sorted by their Alexa rank&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Devin Price has updated his &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptheming.com/2014/08/theme-shop-directory-2014/&quot;&gt;list of WordPress theme shops&lt;/a&gt;, sorted by Alexa rank, for 2014. This is a really interesting list that&amp;#8217;s sure to enlighten you to some theme shops that you&amp;#8217;ve never heard of. I&amp;#8217;ve referenced the 2013 version many times in the past. I&amp;#8217;m glad Devin put time into doing this again.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Alexa isn&amp;#8217;t a perfect way to rank theme shops, obviously, but it does offer good insight to see what average Joes unfamiliar with the WordPress theme landscape probably stumble upon as they search for WordPress themes. As Devin notes, the order of the top shops haven&amp;#8217;t changed a whole lot in the past year, though pretty much all have gained ground, and WPMU Dev jumped all the way to number 1 from number 6.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Hub and spoke versus distributed teams&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Jeff Chandler blogged about &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/how-crowd-favorite-utilizes-multiple-offices-and-a-distributed-work-force&quot;&gt;Crowd Favorite&amp;#8217;s &lt;del&gt;hub and spoke office&lt;/del&gt; (&lt;em&gt;edit&lt;/em&gt;: it&amp;#8217;s actually a constellation model; no &amp;#8220;hub&amp;#8221;) model&lt;/a&gt; (a central office + many smaller offices). Jake Goldman responded with his &lt;a href=&quot;http://jakegoldman.me/2014/08/hub-and-spoke-vs-distributed/&quot;&gt;case for a fully distributed team&lt;/a&gt; (10up&amp;#8217;s model). Both offer quality insight into how some of the larger WordPress consultancies operate.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;You can&amp;#8217;t afford the plugin you want&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Chris Lema has written &lt;a href=&quot;http://chrislema.com/cant-afford-wordpress-plugin-want/&quot;&gt;an excellent post about custom plugin development&lt;/a&gt;, and why you just can&amp;#8217;t get the exact thing you want off the shelf (unless you get real lucky).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;That plugin that does everything you ever wanted? It doesn’t exist. And if it did, if someone built it, it would cost you thousands and thousands of dollars.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Because what you often describe isn’t a plugin. It’s a system.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;And since you don’t want to connect several focused plugins, that each do the one thing they were made to do, you won’t really find the perfect plugin sitting there waiting for you.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;SSL all the things&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;more-7070&quot;&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://searchengineland.com/google-starts-giving-ranking-boost-secure-httpsssl-sites-199446&quot;&gt;Google spoke from on high&lt;/a&gt;, declaring SSL to be a portion of their ranking algorithm. The SEOs and the SSL sellers rejoiced. Tim Nash has a nice&lt;a href=&quot;https://timnash.co.uk/guessing-ssl-questions/&quot;&gt; primer on the nerdy details of SSL&lt;/a&gt;. Joost de Valk also has some &lt;a href=&quot;https://yoast.com/move-website-https-ssl/&quot;&gt;practical tips for switching over to SSL&lt;/a&gt;. And Zack Tollman has a great performance post over at The Theme Foundry &lt;a href=&quot;https://thethemefoundry.com/blog/why-we-dont-use-a-cdn-spdy-ssl/&quot;&gt;about SPDY and SSL&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Now, all that said, seriously don&amp;#8217;t freak out about SSL. It is great, that&amp;#8217;s true, but just because Google says it&amp;#8217;s part of their algorithm doesn&amp;#8217;t mean you have to have it no matter what. Still though, having SSL enabled is probably a good thing for most sites, if you can afford it. Just be smart about it, and not purely reactionary to Google&amp;#8217;s whims.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Some hosts start to support Clef, the password-less login app&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;SiteGround and three other hosts announced &lt;a href=&quot;http://blog.getclef.com/protecting-users-default/&quot;&gt;default support for Clef last week&lt;/a&gt;. New installs on those platforms will enable the password-less login app. Clef works as a form of two-factor authentication, since you have to have your phone on you and scan the login screen to access the site.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;It&amp;#8217;s obviously past time to rely purely on passwords, so it&amp;#8217;s good to see folks supporting Clef and other two-factor methods out of the box.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;WordPress-based portfolio templates, with Semplice&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://semplicelabs.com/&quot;&gt;Semplice&lt;/a&gt; is a WordPress portfolio template product, that&amp;#8217;s still in development, but it&amp;#8217;s definitely outside of the normal WordPress themes you see. I got in touch with the folks behind Semplice and they expect to have something ready in a few weeks for beta testing. It seems you can already buy it though, so I don&amp;#8217;t know what that&amp;#8217;s about. Either way, this may be a product to keep an eye on.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;The WordPress security &amp;#8220;delimma&amp;#8221;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Tony Perez, CEO of Sucuri, write about &lt;a href=&quot;http://tonyonsecurity.com/2014/08/09/the-dilemma-that-is-wordpress-security/&quot;&gt;what he considers to be a delimma with WordPress security&lt;/a&gt;. I don&amp;#8217;t personally agree with some of Tony&amp;#8217;s conclusions here, but they are worth reading, as your mileage may vary. He takes some folks&amp;#8217; words to task (including my own), but I think in the end there is a more a difference in opinion on how to delivery the security message versus actual differences in implementing security measures.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I believe the Drupal vs WordPress method for highlighting last week&amp;#8217;s security release was a reflection of how WordPress and Drupal communicate in general; WordPress said it as if speaking to regular site owners and Drupal spoke to developers. To me, making WordPress accessible to regular people is paramount &amp;#8212; related to security issues or not.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I have a lot more I can say about this, but I have no desire to get in a pointless battle when I think we mostly agree on the goal, just not the message. But I do have one more note. Tony finishes his post with this:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;You can’t own 22% of the market and not expect issues. Is it best to fight it and blindly convince yourself that they don’t exist, or is it better to embrace it?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I take exception to this. I don&amp;#8217;t know anyone in a significant position within the WordPress project that takes such a &amp;#8220;blind&amp;#8221; stance. You can&amp;#8217;t say WordPress core developers don&amp;#8217;t take security seriously, because they absolutely do.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Stellar and international payments&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://www.stellar.org/blog/introducing-stellar/&quot;&gt;Stellar&lt;/a&gt; is a &amp;#8220;a decentralized protocol for sending and receiving money in any pair of currencies&amp;#8221; with some big backers, like Stripe. Brent and Kirby, at Prospress, nerded out over Stellar when it launched, and then wrote up a &lt;a href=&quot;http://prospress.com/will-stellar-finally-fix-international-payments/&quot;&gt;great post about what this could mean for big savings in international eCommerce&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Tablesaw: responsive tables, by Filament Group&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Responsive tables are a pain. The Filament Group really attacked them with &lt;a href=&quot;http://filamentgroup.com/lab/tablesaw.html&quot;&gt;Tablesaw&lt;/a&gt;. This is a really nice solution that you may consider for implementation with certain types of themes and websites.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Comment likes on WordPress.com&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://en.blog.wordpress.com/2014/08/07/introducing-comment-likes/&quot;&gt;WordPress.com has introduced comment likes&lt;/a&gt;. This could be great for some sites with heavy amounts of comments, especially if they add some sorting options to bring good comments to the top. It might be a while before this one hits Jetpack though; apparently there are some technical challenges there.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Get news of new WordPress.com themes&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Also in WordPress.com land, it turns out they aren&amp;#8217;t really blogging about every theme release any more. So Luke McDonald put together a Twitter account to help keep you informed.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot; width=&quot;550&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://t.co/unxO0Vbjaz&quot;&gt;http://t.co/unxO0Vbjaz&lt;/a&gt; no longer promotes or announces Premium theme releases, so I spent some time to do this: &lt;a href=&quot;https://t.co/Cenf4RW0Ed&quot;&gt;https://t.co/Cenf4RW0Ed&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; Luke McDonald (@thelukemcdonald) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/thelukemcdonald/statuses/497817557529665536&quot;&gt;August 8, 2014&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Why attend WordPress conferences (and updates on some of them)&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Andy Leverenz puts some good reasons together on the Elegant Themes blog about &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.elegantthemes.com/blog/tips-tricks/wordpress-conferences-are-on-the-rise-why-you-should-attend&quot;&gt;why you should attend WordPress conferences&lt;/a&gt;, and he highlights some of those coming up.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Speaking of, if you want to go to PressNomics (the attendee list is awesome so far), &lt;a href=&quot;http://pressnomics.com/2014/08/players-came-far-wide-attendees/&quot;&gt;you better act soon&lt;/a&gt;; that conference could sell out really soon.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The &lt;a href=&quot;http://2014.sf.wordcamp.org/2014/08/04/say-hello-to-the-first-group-of-wordcamp-san-francisco-speakers/&quot;&gt;first&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://2014.sf.wordcamp.org/2014/08/07/our-second-group-of-wordcamp-san-francisco-speakers/&quot;&gt;second&lt;/a&gt; batches of WordCamp San Francisco speakers have been announced.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://2014.europe.wordcamp.org/&quot;&gt;WordCamp Europe&amp;#8217;s&lt;/a&gt; speaker list is also dripping out, and it&amp;#8217;s pretty amazing; that&amp;#8217;s going to be an incredible event in Sofia.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Finally, if you&amp;#8217;re in the south, WordCamp Birmingham (my local camp &amp;#8212; #WPYall!) is this Saturday. It&amp;#8217;s going to be a great time, and I hope I get to meet some of you there. You can still register, &lt;a href=&quot;http://2014.birmingham.wordcamp.org/&quot;&gt;so do that and come learn with us&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;hr /&gt;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:49:&quot;WordPress.tv: WordCamp Program and Guidelines AMA&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wordpress.tv/?p=36468&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:67:&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2014/08/10/wordcamp-program-and-guidelines-ama/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:641:&quot;&lt;div id=&quot;v-GpOXhwFM-1&quot; class=&quot;video-player&quot;&gt;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:81:&quot;WordPress.tv: Brennen Byrne: Passwords – The Weakest Link in WordPress Security&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wordpress.tv/?p=37133&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:96:&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2014/08/10/brennen-byrne-passwords-the-weakest-link-in-wordpress-security-3/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:712:&quot;&lt;div id=&quot;v-zHKcIQfo-1&quot; class=&quot;video-player&quot;&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;  &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; href=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/gocomments/wptv.wordpress.com/37133/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/comments/wptv.wordpress.com/37133/&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt; &lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://pixel.wp.com/b.gif?host=wordpress.tv&amp;blog=5089392&amp;post=37133&amp;subd=wptv&amp;ref=&amp;feed=1&quot; width=&quot;1&quot; height=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2014/08/10/brennen-byrne-passwords-the-weakest-link-in-wordpress-security-3/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Brennen Byrne: Passwords &amp;#8211; The Weakest Link in WordPress Security&quot; src=&quot;http://videos.videopress.com/zHKcIQfo/video-4a4789c1c2_scruberthumbnail_1.jpg&quot; width=&quot;160&quot; height=&quot;120&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Sun, 10 Aug 2014 15:02:53 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;WordPress.tv&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:24;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:24:&quot;Matt: Exploring Ubiquiti&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:21:&quot;http://ma.tt/?p=43979&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:40:&quot;http://ma.tt/2014/08/exploring-ubiquiti/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:5846:&quot;&lt;p&gt;I was looking for something else when I stumbled across &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.amazon.com/dp/B00CPRVF5K/&quot;&gt;a little $95 router&lt;/a&gt; that claimed it could do 1M packets per second, multi-WAN, was tiny, and had 80 5-star reviews. Huh? The reviews had some left-handed compliments (&amp;#8220;for advanced users only&amp;#8221;) but one mentioned getting hooked on the company&amp;#8217;s other products as well. Next thing I know I&amp;#8217;m looking at a &lt;a href=&quot;http://amazon.com/dp/B004XXMUCQ/&quot;&gt;$67 access point&lt;/a&gt; that has everyone raving about its range and extensibility. These things were too cheap &amp;#8212; my assumption was it was a Chinese OEM like &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.zyxel.com/&quot;&gt;Zyxel&lt;/a&gt; that makes novel but ultimately not the best quality products.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;At this point I should confess I&amp;#8217;m a bit of a consumer networking geek &amp;#8212; it&amp;#8217;s a hobby of mine. I really enjoy upgrading people&amp;#8217;s routers so they have better range in parts of the house they didn&amp;#8217;t before, getting them a &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B007IMPMW4/&quot;&gt;DOCSIS 3.0 modem&lt;/a&gt; so their connection is faster (and buying it so they don&amp;#8217;t pay an exorbitant rental fee to their cable company), everything about &lt;a href=&quot;http://sonos.com/&quot;&gt;Sonos&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.sonos.com/airplay/&quot;&gt;hooking up an Airport Express to Sonos so you can Airplay things&lt;/a&gt;, showing how you can set up two APs with the same SSID and clients will just connect to whatever they&amp;#8217;re closest to, you don&amp;#8217;t need each one to have a unique SSID, you can give the 2.4ghz and 5ghz networks the same SSID, Time Machine for backups, setting up failover internet with multiple connections or a USB LTE stick&amp;#8230; I redo all my home stuff about once every 18 months, and then take the best of what I&amp;#8217;ve learned and set up friends. I&amp;#8217;m constantly updating firmware. My current best practice setup is &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.sonos.com/&quot;&gt;Sonos&lt;/a&gt; for all audio, usually streaming from &lt;a href=&quot;http://spotify.com/&quot;&gt;Spotify&lt;/a&gt; or &lt;a href=&quot;http://siriusxm.com/&quot;&gt;SiriusXM&lt;/a&gt;, a &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.amazon.com/dp/B00I9RQOR4/&quot;&gt;Peplink Balance One router&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.amazon.com/dp/B00F0DD0I6/&quot;&gt;Netgear Nighthawk R9000 access points&lt;/a&gt; (though I liked the &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.amazon.com/dp/B008ABOJKS/&quot;&gt;ASUS AC66U just as much&lt;/a&gt;), if I need a switch I&amp;#8217;ll go for &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B004GHMU5Q/&quot;&gt;a higher-end managed one&lt;/a&gt; that support spanning tree protocol (STP) properly because otherwise the way the Sonos does bridging can spaz out and overload your network, &lt;a href=&quot;https://nest.com/&quot;&gt;Nest themostat and smoke detectors&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.smartthings.com/&quot;&gt;Smartthings&lt;/a&gt; for everything else. I&amp;#8217;m &lt;a href=&quot;http://august.com/&quot;&gt;waiting for August&lt;/a&gt; for smart locks.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;At the &lt;a href=&quot;http://automattic.com/&quot;&gt;Automattic&lt;/a&gt; office we run &lt;a href=&quot;https://meraki.cisco.com/&quot;&gt;Meraki&lt;/a&gt;, which was pretty solid until we upgraded to the MR34 to get 802.11AC, but it&amp;#8217;s expensive, and you need to subscribe to a per-device yearly license fee for everything to work. They also have &lt;a href=&quot;https://meraki.cisco.com/blog/&quot;&gt;a great WP-powered blog&lt;/a&gt;, and generally the cleanest site of anyone out there. That said, they&amp;#8217;re impossible to buy without going through a terrible reseller, so I&amp;#8217;ve never been able to justify using it at home.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Back to Ubiquiti. First I come across their &lt;a href=&quot;http://community.ubnt.com/&quot;&gt;forums/community sites&lt;/a&gt;, which are ugly and sprawling and full of amazing info from people who do wireless deployments across all of the top companies like &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.arubanetworks.com/&quot;&gt;Aruba&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.ruckuswireless.com/&quot;&gt;Ruckus&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.aerohive.com/&quot;&gt;Aerohive&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.xirrus.com/&quot;&gt;Xirrus&lt;/a&gt;, Meraki. You see people making builds for &lt;a href=&quot;http://community.ubnt.com/t5/EdgeMAX/EdgeRouter-and-Xbox-LIVE/m-p/640951#M18782&quot;&gt;alternative UPNP packages&lt;/a&gt; and that going into their core release months later. (Everything is Debian based, from what I can tell.) The company is based in San Jose that went public a few years ago, and is &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.google.com/finance?q=NASDAQ%3AUBNT&quot;&gt;now worth about 3.7B&lt;/a&gt;, and the founder (formerly of Apple) &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.businessweek.com/articles/2013-04-24/robert-pera-the-kid-that-bought-the-grizzlies&quot;&gt;bought the Memphis Grizzlies&lt;/a&gt;. They seem to have gotten their start with long-haul point-to-point wireless radios &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.ubnt.com/airfiber/airfiber5/&quot;&gt;that can go dozens of kilometers&lt;/a&gt;, which makes sense why their APs would be known for their range. You can buy direct from them, or like I mentioned most of their stuff is available on Amazon. And it&amp;#8217;s inexpensive! Even Ubiquiti&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;http://amazon.com/gp/product/B00D80J2XU/&quot;&gt;AC product, which is $300,&lt;/a&gt; is much, much cheaper than the Meraki MR34 which costs $1,400 and requires a yearly license &lt;em&gt;or it stops working&lt;/em&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Plus they make these wonderfully cheesy product promo videos:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;embed-youtube&quot;&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Normally I wouldn&amp;#8217;t post about something until I&amp;#8217;ve tried it in-person, but I was excited to find this whole new (to me) world of high-performance, reasonable-cost devices. John Pozazidides, long-time WP community member, did &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vj_nlSWGkb8&quot;&gt;an overview of the Unifi devices on Youtube&lt;/a&gt;. At Automattic our once-a-year grand meetup is coming up in Utah, and every year wireless is an issue, especially the first day or two. I ordered some of the Ubiquiti equipment to test when I&amp;#8217;m in Houston next week, looking forward to playing around with it.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Any Ma.tt readers with experience with any of these or big WLAN deployments?&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Sat, 09 Aug 2014 19:02:03 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:14:&quot;Matt Mullenweg&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:25;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:65:&quot;WPTavern: WordPress cdnjs Plugin Makes It Easy to Offload Scripts&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=28012&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:174:&quot;http://wptavern.com/wordpress-cdnjs-plugin-makes-it-easy-to-offload-scripts?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=wordpress-cdnjs-plugin-makes-it-easy-to-offload-scripts&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3173:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/wp-cdnjs.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28012]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/wp-cdnjs.png?resize=772%2C250&quot; alt=&quot;wp-cdnjs&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28020&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The &lt;a href=&quot;http://cdnjs.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;cdnjs&lt;/a&gt; service is used by hundreds of thousands of websites to offload static files for performance. It&amp;#8217;s an open source community-driven project that hosts a variety of different file types, including JavaScript, CSS, SWF, and images, thanks to help from sponsors UserApp and CloudFlare.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/wp-cdnjs/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WP cdnjs&lt;/a&gt; is a new plugin that allows users to easily include any CSS or JavaScript library hosted at cdnjs. Once installed, you can search all cdnjs libraries directly within the plugin&amp;#8217;s settings.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/search-cdnjs.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28012]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/search-cdnjs.png?resize=1025%2C586&quot; alt=&quot;search-cdnjs&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28026&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Once you locate a script you want to use, you have the option to choose secondary assets and select the minified/non-minified version. Scripts can be enabled and even re-ordered on the settings page.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/add-scripts.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[28012]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/add-scripts.png?resize=1025%2C582&quot; alt=&quot;add-scripts&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28028&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The plugin adds the libraries using &lt;a href=&quot;http://paulirish.com/2010/the-protocol-relative-url/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;protocol-relative URLs&lt;/a&gt; which means that it will support both http and https sites.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Although the settings page looks very simple, WP cdnjs packs in a solid set of features:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Builtin cdnjs.com search&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Reorder included files with an intuitive drag-and-drop interface&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Integrates seamlessly with WordPress (no developer up-sells or donation requests)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Choose the secondary assets you want to include&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Selects the minified version or non-minified version&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Optionally select any additional assets you&amp;#8217;d like&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Specify where to include files (header / footer)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Options to globally or individually enable and disable included libraries&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;SSL support
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I tested the plugin and was impressed by how easy it was to find and use libraries. cdnjs is a useful and dependable service that generally operates with &lt;a href=&quot;http://stats.pingdom.com/htbkuegtgycv&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;99.9% uptime&lt;/a&gt;. This plugin makes it easy and convenient for WordPress admins take advantage of the free CDN. If you want to offload some commonly used scripts, chances are that you&amp;#8217;ll find them at cdnjs. Download &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/wp-cdnjs/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WP cdnjs&lt;/a&gt; from WordPress.org and start searching for libraries that you can offload to improve performance.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Fri, 08 Aug 2014 23:55:11 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:30;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:64:&quot;WordPress.tv: How to upload your WordCamp videos to WordPress.tv&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wordpress.tv/?p=37731&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:82:&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2014/08/08/how-to-upload-your-wordcamp-videos-to-wordpress-tv/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:677:&quot;&lt;div id=&quot;v-88YRYWc5-1&quot; class=&quot;video-player&quot;&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;  &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; href=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/gocomments/wptv.wordpress.com/37731/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/comments/wptv.wordpress.com/37731/&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt; &lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://pixel.wp.com/b.gif?host=wordpress.tv&amp;blog=5089392&amp;post=37731&amp;subd=wptv&amp;ref=&amp;feed=1&quot; width=&quot;1&quot; height=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2014/08/08/how-to-upload-your-wordcamp-videos-to-wordpress-tv/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;How to upload your WordCamp videos to WordPress.tv&quot; src=&quot;http://videos.videopress.com/88YRYWc5/video-d78811a062_scruberthumbnail_0.jpg&quot; width=&quot;160&quot; height=&quot;120&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Fri, 08 Aug 2014 22:56:06 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;WordPress.tv&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:31;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:78:&quot;WPTavern: Heroku WP: A Template for Installing and Running WordPress on Heroku&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=27968&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:198:&quot;http://wptavern.com/heroku-wp-a-template-for-installing-and-running-wordpress-on-heroku?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=heroku-wp-a-template-for-installing-and-running-wordpress-on-heroku&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3724:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/wp-and-heroku.jpg&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[27968]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/wp-and-heroku.jpg?resize=715%2C302&quot; alt=&quot;wp-and-heroku&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-28002&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Over the past few months, WordPress developers have been experimenting with speeding up PHP execution with HHVM (HipHop Virtual Machine) and have achieved some &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/markjaquith/statuses/458294601129144320&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;amazingly fast load times&lt;/a&gt;. HHVM &lt;a href=&quot;http://hhvm.com/blog/3095/getting-wordpress-running-on-hhvm&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;compatibility with WordPress&lt;/a&gt; is gradually improving and more hosting companies are moving to adopt it, as many believe that HHVM will soon revolutionize PHP.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Changes in WordPress 3.9 helped to improve compatibility with HHVM and, as a result, a few WP + HHVM templates have popped up, including a new one for Heroku fans. &lt;a href=&quot;https://github.com/xyu/heroku-wp&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Heroku WP&lt;/a&gt; is a template for installing and running WordPress on the &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.heroku.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Heroku&lt;/a&gt; cloud application platform with the official Heroku stack.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Automattic engineer &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.xyu.io/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Xiao Yu&lt;/a&gt; created Heroku WP with the goal of keeping it simple, fast, secure, and scalable. He used Heroku&amp;#8217;s new &lt;a href=&quot;https://blog.heroku.com/archives/2014/4/29/introducing_the_new_php_on_heroku&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;PHP buildpack&lt;/a&gt; which incorporates nginx and HHVM. Heroku WP is built on top of the following:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://nginx.org/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;nginx&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; For serving web content&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://hhvm.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;HHVM&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; A virtual machine designed to serve Hack and PHP&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://www.mysql.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;MySQL&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; Provided by the ClearDB add-on&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://memcached.org/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Memcached&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; Provided by the MemCachier add-on&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://getcomposer.org/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Composer&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; A dependency manager to make installing and managing plugins easier&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The Heroku WP template also bundles Jetpack, SendGrid, caching plugins, &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.stackexchange.com/questions/38902&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;SSL Domain Alias&lt;/a&gt; to send WP admin traffic to Heroku over SSL directly, and a couple of other plugins. You can include additional plugins and/or upgrade versions by updating the &lt;code&gt;composer.json&lt;/code&gt; file.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;2.5X Improvement in WordPress Response Times with Heroku WP&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Yu &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.xyu.io/2014/06/wordpress-on-nginx-hhvm-with-heroku-buildpacks/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;reports&lt;/a&gt; that with the new nginx + HHVM Heroku buildpack, his updated template for WordPress has seen more than 2.5X improvement in response times when compared to the old Heroku LAMP stack. His personal &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.xyu.io/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;site&lt;/a&gt; is actually running on the template. &amp;#8220;It feels a lot faster navigating WP admin and page generation times look much better,&amp;#8221; he said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The template is not just for small blogs. Yu built Heroku WP with cloud architecture in mind, so that &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.heroku.com/pricing&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;the number of Dynos can scale&lt;/a&gt; without breaking. If you&amp;#8217;ve been looking for a quick way to experiment with WordPress on NGINX + HHVM, the Heroku WP template is an excellent starting point. Follow Yu&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;https://github.com/xyu/heroku-wp#installation&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;instructions&lt;/a&gt; for installing, configuring and deploying WordPress to Heroku.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Fri, 08 Aug 2014 21:20:59 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:32;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:83:&quot;WPTavern: How Crowd Favorite Utilizes Multiple Offices and a Distributed Work Force&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=27870&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:210:&quot;http://wptavern.com/how-crowd-favorite-utilizes-multiple-offices-and-a-distributed-work-force?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=how-crowd-favorite-utilizes-multiple-offices-and-a-distributed-work-force&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:7086:&quot;&lt;p&gt;As I was listening to an &lt;a title=&quot;http://www.poststat.us/chris-lema-interview/&quot; href=&quot;http://www.poststat.us/chris-lema-interview/&quot;&gt;interview with Chris Lema&lt;/a&gt;, I was surprised to hear how Crowd Favorite has offices setup across the world. Many of the WordPress agencies I&amp;#8217;m familiar with are 100% distributed with one physical office. This is the first time I&amp;#8217;ve heard of a WordPress development agency with multiple offices throughout the world. I contacted the CTO of &lt;a title=&quot;http://crowdfavorite.com&quot; href=&quot;http://crowdfavorite.com&quot;&gt;Crowd Favorite&lt;/a&gt;, Chris Lema, to learn why the company is structured this way and what practical benefits and drawbacks it offers.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;The Crowd Favorite Approach To Offices&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/CrowdFavoriteOfficesAcrossTheWorld.jpg&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[27870]&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-27963&quot; src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/CrowdFavoriteOfficesAcrossTheWorld.jpg?resize=1025%2C332&quot; alt=&quot;Crowd Favorite Office Locations Across The World&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Crowd Favorite Office Locations Across The World
&lt;p&gt;Crowd Favorite takes an entirely different approach to having an office. Instead of one or two locations, they have small, satellite offices spread across the world. This approach allows the company to merge the benefits of a distributed work force with having physical locations. Each office is staffed by a group of people who excel at a specific skill. Lema describes the offices as &lt;em&gt;communities of practice&lt;/em&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;For example, there&amp;#8217;s an office in Phoenix that we have that is dedicated to design work and branding, and they&amp;#8217;re fantastic at that. That&amp;#8217;s a very different dynamic than if you had three designers across the country, four designers across the country, or two brand people across the country.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Sure, if they were really phenomenal people, you could hire them and you&amp;#8217;d get a bang for your buck, but if you put a whole group of them together in one place, you&amp;#8217;ll discover that they go further faster.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Regional and localized offices enable people to work together to accelerate their progress. The offices are also used to focus on disciplines. For example, the Las Vegas, NV office is focused on video and promotion, the office in Arizona is focused on design, and the office in Denver, CO is focused on advanced development. Crowd Favorite even has a small office in New York focused on .net and Ruby development.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Offices Have Different Purposes Depending On The Region&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Offices outside the US have a unique business dynamic associated with them. They&amp;#8217;re used as the final component of a business deal after establishing trust and a relationship with a customer. &amp;#8220;As Karim Marucchi worked in several different countries, it became a cornerstone of the way he works, that he would have an office, and that&amp;#8217;s the office that would drive the business in that region.&amp;#8221; Lema said. &amp;#8220;It&amp;#8217;s especially effective when you think about it on the international stage because you want to be able to make sure that your presence is physically felt in the areas where you&amp;#8217;re doing business. We have an office in Italy for example, specifically for that reason.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;The Lone Rangers Of A Distributed Workforce&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/TheLongRangerWorker.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[27870]&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-27961&quot; src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/TheLongRangerWorker.png?resize=637%2C279&quot; alt=&quot;The Lone Ranger Developer&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;photo credit: &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.flickr.com/photos/eschipul/2296528916/&quot;&gt;eschipul&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; &lt;a href=&quot;http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/2.0/&quot;&gt;cc&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;One of the benefits of having several office locations is the increased opportunity for employees to work together. However, one of the biggest drawbacks is that some employees end up working alone. For example, Crowd Favorite has an office in Seattle, WA that handles development operations that is staffed by one person. This is why Crowd Favorite and other companies with a distributed work force organize company wide meetups once or twice a year. It gives individuals a chance to meet their co-workers and strengthen their connection to the company.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;How Other WordPress Companies Handle Offices&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;One of the benefits of working with WordPress is that it can be done from anywhere in the world, as long as an internet connection is available. &lt;a title=&quot;http://automattic.com/&quot; href=&quot;http://automattic.com/&quot;&gt;Automattic&lt;/a&gt; is a leading example of how employees can accomplish anything without having to spend eight hours in a cubicle. Despite having a distributed work force, the company maintains a physical presence with an office in San Francisco, CA. The office is used as a co-working space, to host shareholder meetings, or to just hang out.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Web development firm &lt;a title=&quot;http://10up.com/&quot; href=&quot;http://10up.com/&quot;&gt;10up &lt;/a&gt;has an office in &lt;a title=&quot;http://10up.com/blog/2013/portland-office-opening/&quot; href=&quot;http://10up.com/blog/2013/portland-office-opening/&quot;&gt;Portland, OR&lt;/a&gt;. The office hosts speakers, out-of-town guests, and the occasional workshop. &lt;a title=&quot;http://webdevstudios.com/&quot; href=&quot;http://webdevstudios.com/&quot;&gt;WebDevStudios&lt;/a&gt; is another large web development firm with a 100% distributed work force. Unlike 10up and Automattic, the company has two office locations, one in &lt;a title=&quot;http://webdevstudios.com/about/webdevstudios/new-jersey-location/&quot; href=&quot;http://webdevstudios.com/about/webdevstudios/new-jersey-location/&quot;&gt;New Jersey&lt;/a&gt; and the other in &lt;a title=&quot;http://webdevstudios.com/about/webdevstudios/philadelphia-location/&quot; href=&quot;http://webdevstudios.com/about/webdevstudios/philadelphia-location/&quot;&gt;Philadelphia, PA&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Copy The Motivation, Not The Model&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Going with a 100% distributed work force has drawbacks as does everyone working in the same physical space. Crowd Favorite believes they have figured out a way to reap the benefits of both methods. &amp;#8220;When you say we&amp;#8217;re only going to have one office, there are drawbacks. When you say we&amp;#8217;re going to be 100% remote, there are going to be drawbacks. I think we&amp;#8217;ve tried to thread the needle on this to find the situation that gives us the least amount of drawbacks with the most amount of potential.&amp;#8221; Lema said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Is the way Crowd Favorite uses offices a model for other WordPress development firms to follow? &amp;#8220;Copying someone&amp;#8217;s model is a really poor approach to anything. Copying someone&amp;#8217;s motivation may be a more helpful approach to think about.&amp;#8221; Lema told the Tavern. Every company is different and has to satisfy its own needs and requirements.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Crowd Favorite has found success using offices not only for co-working spaces, but as a way to build trust and establish relationships with clients in other parts of the world.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Fri, 08 Aug 2014 20:25:37 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:33;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;

The event was a huge success, with four full tracks of expert designers, developers, and WordPress professionals sharing what they&amp;#8217;ve learned.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I had a great time with everyone there. I saw old friends, and met new friends.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I had my recording equipment with me, and I asked a question to some folks there: how has WordPress changed your life?&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Here are their answers:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;  &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; href=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/gocomments/wptv.wordpress.com/37121/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/comments/wptv.wordpress.com/37121/&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt; &lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://pixel.wp.com/b.gif?host=wordpress.tv&amp;blog=5089392&amp;post=37121&amp;subd=wptv&amp;ref=&amp;feed=1&quot; width=&quot;1&quot; height=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2014/08/08/stacey-lane-how-to-pick-a-wordpress-theme-that-doesnt-suck/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Stacey Lane: How To Pick a WordPress Theme That Doesn&amp;#8217;t Suck&quot; src=&quot;http://videos.videopress.com/rcIC0zXI/video-f420b5a692_scruberthumbnail_1.jpg&quot; width=&quot;160&quot; height=&quot;120&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Fri, 08 Aug 2014 15:24:32 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;WordPress.tv&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:37;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:69:&quot;WPTavern: Mobile ShareBar Adds a WhatsApp Sharing Button to WordPress&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=24066&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:182:&quot;http://wptavern.com/mobile-sharebar-adds-a-whatsapp-sharing-button-to-wordpress?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=mobile-sharebar-adds-a-whatsapp-sharing-button-to-wordpress&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3635:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Earlier this year, Facebook &lt;a href=&quot;http://newsroom.fb.com/news/2014/02/facebook-to-acquire-whatsapp/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;acquired WhatsApp&lt;/a&gt; for $19 billion dollars. With 450+ million users per month and 70% of them active per day, Facebook is betting on the the app&amp;#8217;s massive user base and continued growth.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Although &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.whatsapp.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WhatsApp&lt;/a&gt; is enormously popular, very few WordPress sharing plugins have prioritized adding the service to the list of supported sharing options. Depending on the demographic of your site&amp;#8217;s readership, you may stand to strongly benefit from making it easy for WhatsApp users to share your content with each other via the app.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/mobile-sharebar/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Mobile ShareBar&lt;/a&gt; is one of the first plugins to add a WhatsApp sharing button, right up there with the same preeminence of Facebook and Twitter. The sharebar only appears to visitors when they are browsing your site on a mobile site, and you can remove the Facebook and Twitter buttons if you just want to include WhatsApp.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/mobile-sharebar-example.jpg&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[24066]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/mobile-sharebar-example.jpg?resize=450%2C694&quot; alt=&quot;mobile-sharebar-example&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-27928&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The plugin allows you to select specific post types where you want the sharebar to appear, i.e. frontpage, posts, pages, categories, archives, tags, and even specific custom post types. You can also change the position of the bar to appear on the bottom of the screen. All text for the sharing buttons is customizable in the plugin&amp;#8217;s settings page:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/mobile-sharebar-options.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[24066]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/mobile-sharebar-options.png?resize=659%2C558&quot; alt=&quot;mobile-sharebar-options&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-27941&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;A real-time preview of the sharebar appears in the settings page as you edit it, so you know what it&amp;#8217;s going to look like on mobile devices. After testing the plugin, my only complaint is that the sharebar is sticky as you scroll down the page, taking up valuable mobile real estate. Having the option to remove that would be preferable, as stickiness might be a deal breaker for some users.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;While WhatsApp is available for iPhone, BlackBerry, Android, Windows Phone and Nokia, the sharing button only works with iPhones at the moment. This is because the iPhone app is the only one that works with the &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.whatsapp.com/faq/iphone/23559013&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;URL scheme&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Facebook CEO Mark Zuckerberg commented on the WhatsApp acquisition: &lt;strong&gt;&amp;#8220;WhatsApp is on a path to connect 1 billion people. The services that reach that milestone are all incredibly valuable.&amp;#8221;&lt;/strong&gt; When &lt;a href=&quot;http://recode.net/2014/02/20/before-facebook-deal-whatsapp-was-helping-buzzfeed-and-shazam-go-viral-with-new-platform-tools/?_ga=1.172310307.1038543520.1407428466&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Buzzfeed added a WhatsApp&lt;/a&gt; sharing button, they found that readers on iOS clicked it more often than the Twitter button. It might be worth finding out if your readers are using WhatsApp so you can prioritize it among your sharing options. You can get the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/mobile-sharebar/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Mobile ShareBar&lt;/a&gt; from WordPress.org.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 07 Aug 2014 23:06:23 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:38;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:81:&quot;WPTavern: How to Change Jetpack Accounts Without Losing Your Stats or Subscribers&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=27914&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:206:&quot;http://wptavern.com/how-to-change-jetpack-accounts-without-losing-your-stats-or-subscribers?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=how-to-change-jetpack-accounts-without-losing-your-stats-or-subscribers&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1732:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/JetpackWordPressStatsFeaturedImage.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[27914]&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;aligncenter wp-image-27924 size-full&quot; src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/JetpackWordPressStatsFeaturedImage.png?resize=669%2C339&quot; alt=&quot;Jetpack Stats Featured Image&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you&amp;#8217;re using Jetpack and need to reconnect it to a site but don&amp;#8217;t have access to the WordPress.com account associated with it, you can switch accounts without losing your stats or subscribers. Just follow these simple steps.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ol&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Login to your self-hosted WordPress site and disconnect Jetpack.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Create a new WordPress.com account.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Connect your self-hosted WordPress site to Jetpack using the new account.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ol&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I asked George Stephanis, who is on the Jetpack development team, if users should be worried about stats and subscribers being lost in the process.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Ideally it should be smooth, and the stats should transfer automatically.  Sites are indexed by domain and path, so as long as those don&amp;#8217;t change and still match up with what we have on file, it&amp;#8217;ll just work.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If they do change and the user winds up connected to a clean site, it&amp;#8217;s just a quick five-minute operation for one of our Happiness Engineers to transfer stats over to the new site, so nothing is ever lost.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In most cases, Jetpack will continue to hum along after switching WordPress.com user accounts. However, if you notice stats missing or weird behavior, you should contact the &lt;a title=&quot;http://jetpack.me/contact-support/&quot; href=&quot;http://jetpack.me/contact-support/&quot;&gt;Jetpack support team&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 07 Aug 2014 21:57:51 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:39;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:87:&quot;WPTavern: Color Posts Plugin Extends Jetpack to Add Intuitive Background Color Matching&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=27889&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:218:&quot;http://wptavern.com/color-posts-plugin-extends-jetpack-to-add-intuitive-background-color-matching?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=color-posts-plugin-extends-jetpack-to-add-intuitive-background-color-matching&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4410:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Automatically changing the background color of a post based on its images is a fancy effect that you may have noticed on WordPress.com&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;http://theme.wordpress.com/themes/ryu/&quot;&gt;Ryu&lt;/a&gt; theme. It&amp;#8217;s currently WordPress.com&amp;#8217;s 7th most popular theme and is also &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/themes/ryu&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;available for self-hosted sites&lt;/a&gt; with the same intuitive background changing feature built in.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/color-posts.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[27889]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/color-posts.png?resize=687%2C597&quot; alt=&quot;color-posts&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-27907&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Jetpack developer &lt;a href=&quot;http://jeremy.hu/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Jeremy Herve&lt;/a&gt; just released an independent plugin version of the feature cut out of the theme. &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/color-posts/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Color Posts&lt;/a&gt; does the following:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ol&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Grabs an image from the post&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Samples it&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Creates a matching color and a contrast value (black or white)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Changes the post&amp;#8217;s background color to match the image&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ol&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/jetpack/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Jetpack&lt;/a&gt; must be active in order for Color Posts to do its magic, as it utilizes the &lt;code&gt;Tonesque&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;Jetpack_PostImages&lt;/code&gt; classes.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Here&amp;#8217;s how it works: Color Posts uses the &lt;code&gt;Jetpack_PostImages&lt;/code&gt; class to run through a few different methods to select an image representative of the post. &lt;a href=&quot;https://github.com/Automattic/jetpack/blob/3.1/_inc/lib/tonesque.php&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Tonesque&lt;/a&gt; grabs the color index for each of five sample points of the image and then finds the average color of the image based on those five sample points. It creates a color object and checks the contrast against the main color, giving either black or white for use with opacity.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The result is beautifully matching backgrounds for each post. The &lt;a href=&quot;http://ryudemo.wordpress.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Ryu theme demo&lt;/a&gt; is a good example of this feature in action.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Extend Color Posts to Color Match Other Elements on Your Site&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/color-matching.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[27889]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/color-matching.png?resize=1025%2C468&quot; alt=&quot;photo credit: Telstar Logistics - cc&quot; class=&quot;size-full wp-image-27917&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;photo credit: &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.flickr.com/photos/telstar/2903029/&quot;&gt;Telstar Logistics&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; &lt;a href=&quot;http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc/2.0/&quot;&gt;cc&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Herve explains in the plugin&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/color-posts/faq/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;FAQ&lt;/a&gt; how it can be used for more than just matching the background of a post to an image. The color matching feature can be applied to post links, image borders, title, etc. He includes example code for building your own CSS from the colors grabbed by the plugin to change other elements on your site.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Herve&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;http://jeremy.hu/color-posts-jetpack-plugin/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;post&lt;/a&gt; gives you an example of how he changes the color and contrast of the title on his site based on the values retrieved by the plugin. If you want to use your own image, instead of letting Jetpack pick, Color Posts lets you do that via the &lt;code&gt;colorposts_image_output&lt;/code&gt; filter. The plugin also lets you change the default color assigned to posts without an image using the &lt;code&gt;jetpack_open_graph_image_default&lt;/code&gt; filter.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Theme developers who already support Jetpack can add color matching to their themes using this method or by offering support for the plugin. Color Posts brings post designs alive with self-aware color matching capabilities. You&amp;#8217;d be hard-pressed to do a better job matching your background colors manually each time &amp;#8211; but who would want to? This plugin does it all automatically with a little bit of magic.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/color-posts/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Color Posts&lt;/a&gt; can be downloaded from WordPress.org but be advised that it&amp;#8217;s still a work in progress. You can contribute feedback and code on &lt;a href=&quot;https://github.com/jeherve/color-posts/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;GitHub&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 07 Aug 2014 20:26:05 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:40;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
