&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:94:&quot;WPTavern: WPCore Plugin Manager Adds Update Notifications, Plans to Implement Pro Subscription&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=27827&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:230:&quot;http://wptavern.com/wpcore-plugin-manager-adds-update-notifications-plans-to-implement-pro-subscription?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=wpcore-plugin-manager-adds-update-notifications-plans-to-implement-pro-subscription&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3213:&quot;&lt;p&gt;WPCore &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/wpcore-create-wordpress-plugin-collections-and-install-them-in-one-click&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;launched&lt;/a&gt; less than a month ago and has already gone through several rounds of improvement. The &lt;a href=&quot;https://wpcore.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;app&lt;/a&gt; allows WordPress users to create plugin collections and install them in one click. Most recently, WPCore added &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/wpcore-plugin-manager-adds-favoriting-and-custom-plugins-to-collections&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;favoriting and the ability to include custom plugins&lt;/a&gt; hosted outside of WordPress.org.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Today, WPCore creator &lt;a href=&quot;http://stueynet.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Stuart Starr&lt;/a&gt; announced a new update notifications feature which allows users to receive email notices when one of their collections has a plugin with an update.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/update-notifications.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[27827]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/update-notifications.png?resize=1025%2C512&quot; alt=&quot;update-notifications&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-27858&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The feature is still in development so it currently sends a separate email for each collection where you have subscriptions enabled. Starr is working on creating a digest email instead. This is a handy feature if you have a site using a collection that includes a plugin you&amp;#8217;re watching for updates. Perhaps you&amp;#8217;re looking for a bug fix or a particular improvement that&amp;#8217;s coming down the line. Turn on email notifications for a collection including the plugin you&amp;#8217;re watching and you&amp;#8217;ll get a notice in your inbox when it&amp;#8217;s time to update.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;WPCore Pro Subscription Plan Coming August 31&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The WPCore site is now SSL secured in preparation for a new paid subscription plan that will be in place on August 31. Starr is electing to thank WPCore&amp;#8217;s early adopters by grandfathering them into the pro account level, which includes all the features currently in place.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Anyone who registers before the end of August will be a WPCore Pro member for life. Once the pro subscription plan is in place, new free users will be on a basic plan, which doesn&amp;#8217;t include custom plugins or the new update notifications feature. Starr told the Tavern that pricing for the pro account level will be in the range of a few cups of coffee per month.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;WPCore Plugin Manager Plugin Rewritten&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/wpcore/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;plugin&lt;/a&gt; that accompanies WPCore has been completely rewritten to perform better and minimize communication with the app. Starr rebuilt the way the plugin pulls in collections to WordPress sites, so the older version of the plugin will no longer return plugins. If you want to be able to add new collections, you&amp;#8217;ll need to update to the latest version.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Starr has been adding improvements based on user feedback and welcomes feature requests and thoughts on the new subscription model. Follow &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/wpcoreapp&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;@wpcoreapp&lt;/a&gt; on Twitter to send any feedback and stay up to date.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 06 Aug 2014 22:07:15 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:45;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:93:&quot;WPTavern: WordPress 3.9.2 Fixes Security Vulnerabilities, Users Strongly Encouraged To Update&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=27834&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:228:&quot;http://wptavern.com/wordpress-3-9-2-fixes-security-vulnerabilities-users-strongly-encouraged-to-update?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=wordpress-3-9-2-fixes-security-vulnerabilities-users-strongly-encouraged-to-update&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2845:&quot;&lt;p&gt;WordPress users are strongly encouraged to update their sites to 3.9.2 as it&amp;#8217;s a security focused release. According to &lt;a title=&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2014/08/wordpress-3-9-2/&quot; href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2014/08/wordpress-3-9-2/&quot;&gt;the announcement&lt;/a&gt;, 3.9.2 fixes a possible denial of service issue in PHP’s XML processing. The bug was first reported by &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/nirgoldshlager&quot;&gt;Nir Goldshlager&lt;/a&gt; of the Salesforce.com Product Security Team and was fixed by Michael Adams and Andrew Nacin of the WordPress security team. The release was also coordinated with the &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.drupal.org/SA-CORE-2014-004&quot;&gt;Drupal security team&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/WordPressVersionsInUse.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[27834]&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-27861&quot; src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/WordPressVersionsInUse.png?resize=323%2C267&quot; alt=&quot;18.8% Of WordPress Sites Are Running On Version 3.5&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;18.8% Of WordPress Sites Are Running On Version 3.5
&lt;p&gt;Since the vulnerability is present in WordPress 3.5 to 3.9.1, there are several sites that need to be manually updated in order to be protected. Automatic updates for security releases was introduced in WordPress 3.7, leaving users of 3.6 and 3.5 especially vulnerable. According to &lt;a title=&quot;https://wordpress.org/about/stats/&quot; href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/about/stats/&quot;&gt;stats on WordPress.org&lt;/a&gt;, 26.8% of all WordPress sites will not be auto updated. Among those sites, 18.8% are still using WordPress 3.5.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 3.9.2 has a few other security updates as well:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Fixes a possible but unlikely code execution when processing widgets (WordPress is not affected by default), discovered by &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.buayacorp.com/&quot;&gt;Alex Concha&lt;/a&gt; of the WordPress security team.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Prevents information disclosure via XML entity attacks in the external GetID3 library, reported by &lt;a href=&quot;http://onsec.ru/en/&quot;&gt;Ivan Novikov&lt;/a&gt; of ONSec.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Adds protections against brute attacks against CSRF tokens, reported by &lt;a href=&quot;http://systemoverlord.com/&quot;&gt;David Tomaschik&lt;/a&gt; of the Google Security Team.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Contains some additional security hardening, like preventing cross-site scripting that could be triggered only by administrators.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;You can update to 3.9.2 immediately by browsing to &lt;strong&gt;Dashboard &amp;gt; Updates &lt;/strong&gt;in the backend of WordPress. Sites that have automatic updates configured will be updated within 12 hours. Sites using WordPress 3.8.3 or 3.7.3 will be updated to 3.8.4 or 3.7.4. Older versions of WordPress are not supported, so please update to 3.9.2 for the latest and greatest.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;It&amp;#8217;s awesome to see the security teams from both WordPress and Drupal working together to keep users safe.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 06 Aug 2014 20:07:01 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:46;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:86:&quot;Post Status: WordPress and Drupal teams collaborate for simultaneous security releases&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:30:&quot;http://www.poststat.us/?p=7020&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:174:&quot;http://www.poststat.us/wordpress-and-drupal-collaborate-for-security-release/?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=wordpress-and-drupal-collaborate-for-security-release&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3367:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;aligncenter size-large wp-image-7024&quot; src=&quot;http://www.poststat.us/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/wordpress-drupal-security1-752x353.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;wordpress-drupal-security&quot; width=&quot;752&quot; height=&quot;353&quot; /&gt;WordPress and Drupal are both releasing security updates today that affect all supported versions of the two popular CMS platforms.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/Nirgoldshlager&quot;&gt;Nir Goldshlager&lt;/a&gt;, a security researcher and part of the Salesforce.com Product Security Team, discovered a PHP-level vulnerability that could result in denial of service (DoS) attacks. Goldshlager notified the PHP, WordPress, and Drupal security teams all at once.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The vulnerability is within a PHP XML parser used by XML-RPC, and is &amp;#8220;vulnerable to an XML entity expansion attach which can cause CPU and memory exhaustion, and MySQL to reach the maximum amount of open connections.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The bug itself is relatively minor, but of interest is the collaboration between the WordPress and Drupal teams to create a fix. WordPress lead developer Andrew Nacin and Mike Adams of the WordPress security team collaborated on a fix for the vulnerability and offered to coordinate with the Drupal security team.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The fix devised by Nacin and Adams prevents the XML-RPC vulnerability while keeping the feature active. Turning off XML-RPC would have left the burden of handling the fix on the site owner or host and would have harmed clients such as the mobile apps.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;So, interestingly enough, two WordPress core developers are getting props today for both WordPress and Drupal releases. The respective security teams and Goldshlager have been working together for a couple of weeks now to appropriately address the situation and refine the patch included in today&amp;#8217;s updates. The patch itself is for an external library that WordPress has always used, called the Incutio XML-RPC Library. Drupal uses a derivative of the same library, making the collaboration between the two teams quite logical and straightforward.&lt;span id=&quot;more-7020&quot;&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Andrew Nacin tells me that this is the first time he knows of that the WordPress and Drupal security teams have collaborated. It certainly goes to show just how beneficial open source is, that two completely different CMS platforms are able to quickly close such security holes.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The WordPress security release includes a few other minor security patches as well, but the collaboration between the WordPress and Drupal security teams is what makes this release most noteworthy, in my opinion.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress will be automatically upgrading all eligible websites from WordPress 3.7 to WordPress 3.9 major versions to include these fixes, as well as the WordPress 4.0 beta. The latest stable branch is now WordPress 3.9.2, and the WordPress 4.0 development branch is in beta 3. The release of WordPress 4.0 is still on target for the week of August 25th.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you have automatic updates enabled for WordPress, you&amp;#8217;ll see those roll out shortly; otherwise, you can download it from &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/download/&quot;&gt;WordPress.org&lt;/a&gt;. You can also check out the official release posts for both &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.drupal.org/SA-CORE-2014-004&quot;&gt;Drupal&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2014/08/wordpress-3-9-2/&quot;&gt;WordPress&lt;/a&gt; on their respective blogs.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 06 Aug 2014 19:05:02 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:15:&quot;Brian Krogsgard&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:47;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:42:&quot;Dev Blog: WordPress 3.9.2 Security Release&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:33:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/?p=3269&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:50:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2014/08/wordpress-3-9-2/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2347:&quot;&lt;p&gt;WordPress 3.9.2 is now available as a security release for all previous versions. We strongly encourage you to update your sites immediately.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This release fixes a possible denial of service issue in PHP&amp;#8217;s XML processing, reported by &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/nirgoldshlager&quot;&gt;Nir Goldshlager&lt;/a&gt; of the Salesforce.com Product Security Team. It  was fixed by Michael Adams and Andrew Nacin of the WordPress security team and David Rothstein of the &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.drupal.org/SA-CORE-2014-004&quot;&gt;Drupal security team&lt;/a&gt;. This is the first time our two projects have coordinated joint security releases.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 3.9.2 also contains other security changes:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Fixes a possible but unlikely code execution when processing widgets (WordPress is not affected by default), discovered by &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.buayacorp.com/&quot;&gt;Alex Concha&lt;/a&gt; of the WordPress security team.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Prevents information disclosure via XML entity attacks in the external GetID3 library, reported by &lt;a href=&quot;http://onsec.ru/en/&quot;&gt;Ivan Novikov&lt;/a&gt; of ONSec.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Adds protections against brute attacks against CSRF tokens, reported by &lt;a href=&quot;http://systemoverlord.com/&quot;&gt;David Tomaschik&lt;/a&gt; of the Google Security Team.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Contains some additional security hardening, like preventing cross-site scripting that could be triggered only by administrators.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We appreciated responsible disclosure of these issues directly to our security team. For more information, see the &lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/Version_3.9.2&quot;&gt;release notes&lt;/a&gt; or consult the &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/log/branches/3.9?stop_rev=29383&amp;rev=29411&quot;&gt;list of changes&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/download/&quot;&gt;Download WordPress 3.9.2&lt;/a&gt; or venture over to &lt;strong&gt;Dashboard → Updates&lt;/strong&gt; and simply click &amp;#8220;Update Now&amp;#8221;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Sites that support automatic background updates will be updated to WordPress 3.9.2 within 12 hours. (If you are still on WordPress 3.8.3 or 3.7.3, you will also be updated to 3.8.4 or 3.7.4. We don&amp;#8217;t support older versions, so please update to 3.9.2 for the latest and greatest.)&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Already testing WordPress 4.0? The third beta is &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/wordpress-4.0-beta3.zip&quot;&gt;now available&lt;/a&gt; (zip) and it contains these security fixes.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 06 Aug 2014 19:04:27 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;Andrew Nacin&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:48;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:79:&quot;WPTavern: MarkPress Plugin Transforms WordPress into a Markdown-Powered Journal&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=27815&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:202:&quot;http://wptavern.com/markpress-plugin-transforms-wordpress-into-a-markdown-powered-journal?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=markpress-plugin-transforms-wordpress-into-a-markdown-powered-journal&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3092:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Over the past year, WordPress plugin developers have created some unique implementations of the post editor that add &lt;a href=&quot;http://daringfireball.net/projects/markdown/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Markdown&lt;/a&gt; editing with a side-by-side preview. Both the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/gust-plugin-adds-support-for-categories-featured-images-and-custom-post-types&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Gust&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptavern.com/splitdown-a-free-ghost-style-markdown-editor-for-wordpress&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Splitdown&lt;/a&gt; plugins were inspired by the &lt;a href=&quot;https://ghost.org/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Ghost&lt;/a&gt; editor and attempt to recreate that experience in WordPress.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/markpress/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;MarkPress&lt;/a&gt; is the newest to join the ranks of Markdown-powered editors. The plugin adds an interesting twist in that it completely transforms your WordPress site to support writing journal notes without being in the admin. The new editor gives a live preview of notes as you compose.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/MarkPress-editor.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[27815]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/MarkPress-editor.png?resize=1025%2C601&quot; alt=&quot;MarkPress-editor&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-27822&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;MarkPress automatically saves as you are writing and naturally only works if the user is logged in. The plugin was designed to work nicely on mobile devices as well. When used on mobile, the top bar displays a button that allows you to toggle back and forth between the compose screen and the preview:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/view-mode.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[27815]&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/view-mode.png?resize=400%2C652&quot; alt=&quot;view-mode&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-27830&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;It&amp;#8217;s important to note that MarkPress takes over your WordPress install on activation and repurposes the frontend for quickly composing journal notes. This isn&amp;#8217;t a plugin that you can use to simply replace the default post editor, as it wasn&amp;#8217;t designed to do that.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;After testing MarkPress I was impressed with its beautiful implementation of the Markdown editor and simplified writing experience. However, finding your way back to the admin after reaching the frontend editor is quite difficult. Additionally, posts are automatically marked as published as you compose them. I understand that MarkPress is focused around journal notes but wish that its beautiful editor could also be used for writing regular blog posts.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Overall, the plugin is nicely done and provides an interesting new take on the WordPress post editor. If you want to create a Markdown-powered journal with WordPress as the sole purpose of your website, then MarkPress is an excellent option that will help you to write more efficiently. &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/plugins/markpress/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Download&lt;/a&gt; it for free from WordPress.org and take it for a test drive.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 06 Aug 2014 18:50:25 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:49;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:56:&quot;WPTavern: Crowd Favorite Announces Chris Lema As New CTO&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wptavern.com/?p=27800&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:156:&quot;http://wptavern.com/crowd-favorite-announces-chris-lema-as-new-cto?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=crowd-favorite-announces-chris-lema-as-new-cto&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4039:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Crowd Favorite &lt;a title=&quot;http://crowdfavorite.com/blog/2014/08/crowd-favorite-welcomes-chris-lema/&quot; href=&quot;http://crowdfavorite.com/blog/2014/08/crowd-favorite-welcomes-chris-lema/&quot;&gt;has appointed Chris Lema&lt;/a&gt; as the company&amp;#8217;s new CTO. Alex King, the current CTO, will move into the Chief Software Architect role, allowing him to focus his expertise in product development and deep-level technical leadership with the company&amp;#8217;s teams. Lema will begin in mid-September and use his product development experience to help bring the WordPress platform and WordPress products into Fortune 500 enterprises.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;How Chris Lema Quickly Became A Leading Figure In The WordPress Community&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/ChrisLemaFeaturedImage.png&quot; rel=&quot;prettyphoto[27800]&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-27802&quot; src=&quot;http://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/ChrisLemaFeaturedImage.png?resize=650%2C200&quot; alt=&quot;Chris Lema Featured Image&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Image Courtesy Of The &lt;a title=&quot;http://2014.miami.wordcamp.org/speaker-submission-update/&quot; href=&quot;http://2014.miami.wordcamp.org/speaker-submission-update/&quot;&gt;WordCamp Miami Website&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;PostStat.us has a &lt;a title=&quot;http://www.poststat.us/chris-lema-interview/&quot; href=&quot;http://www.poststat.us/chris-lema-interview/&quot;&gt;great article covering the move&lt;/a&gt;, including a special one hour interview with Lema. I&amp;#8217;ve jokingly said that Lema has come out of nowhere. Although I still hold to that notion, he explains in the interview, the circumstances that have helped him be successful in the WordPress community.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Lema has years of experience starting, managing, and selling startups especially within the Software as a Service market. With 20 years of experience under his belt, he decided to help others in the WordPress community by sharing stories of the lessons he&amp;#8217;s learned from the mistakes he&amp;#8217;s made &lt;a title=&quot;http://chrislema.com/&quot; href=&quot;http://chrislema.com/&quot;&gt;using his blog&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Since the SaSS and product market in WordPress is so young, his voice and blog quickly became a leading authority. A combination of luck, experience, passion, personality, and timing helped him become an authority in the product space. Writing about the business of WordPress from a perspective not many people have is also a contributing factor.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;A Few Predictions&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Near the end of the interview, Lema makes a few predictions, all of which make sense to me. The first is that WordPress is growing on the edge. These are the people who have heard of WordPress and want to start a website but have no idea where to start. Lema predicts more out of the box solutions for these users. &lt;a title=&quot;http://evermo.re/&quot; href=&quot;http://evermo.re/&quot;&gt;Evermore&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a title=&quot;http://newrainmaker.com/platform/&quot; href=&quot;http://newrainmaker.com/platform/&quot;&gt;Rain Maker&lt;/a&gt;, and &lt;a title=&quot;http://oboxthemes.com/instant&quot; href=&quot;http://oboxthemes.com/instant&quot;&gt;Obox Instant&lt;/a&gt; are just some of the platforms already catering to that segment of the market.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The second is that WordPress businesses will continue to consolidate. Last but not least, product vendors will need to up their game to remain competitive. An example is WordPress hosting. What was once a &lt;strong&gt;wow&lt;/strong&gt; feature two years ago is now a standard feature across most of the basic plans.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;The Voice Of Crowd Favorite&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;With Lema&amp;#8217;s ability to inspire crowds and motivate people with his speaking engagements, I can see him becoming the voice of Crowd Favorite. The announcement post mentions this possibility as well.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;You will continue to hear from us through Chris with his valuable online presence. As a popular speaker at conferences and work with our sales and marketing teams, we know his voice will be a great addition to the Crowd Favorite brand.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I&amp;#8217;ve had the pleasure to speak with Lema at various WordCamps and I can&amp;#8217;t think of a better person to be the voice of a company.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 06 Aug 2014 18:05:18 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}}}}}}}}}}}}s:4:&quot;type&quot;;i:128;s:7:&quot;headers&quot;;a:10:{s:6:&quot;server&quot;;s:5:&quot;nginx&quot;;s:4:&quot;date&quot;;s:29:&quot;Wed, 13 Aug 2014 15:14:01 GMT&quot;;s:12:&quot;content-type&quot;;s:8:&quot;text/xml&quot;;s:14:&quot;content-length&quot;;s:6:&quot;166141&quot;;s:10:&quot;connection&quot;;s:5:&quot;close&quot;;s:4:&quot;vary&quot;;s:15:&quot;Accept-Encoding&quot;;s:13:&quot;last-modified&quot;;s:29:&quot;Wed, 13 Aug 2014 15:00:18 GMT&quot;;s:15:&quot;x-frame-options&quot;;s:10:&quot;SAMEORIGIN&quot;;s:4:&quot;x-nc&quot;;s:11:&quot;HIT lax 250&quot;;s:13:&quot;accept-ranges&quot;;s:5:&quot;bytes&quot;;}s:5:&quot;build&quot;;s:14:&quot;20130910200210&quot;;}</column>

            <column name="post_content">这是示范页面。页面和博客文章不同，它的位置是固定的，通常会在站点导航栏显示。很多用户都创建一个“关于”页面，向访客介绍自己。例如，个人博客通常有类似这样的介绍：

&lt;blockquote&gt;欢迎！我白天是个邮递员，晚上就是个有抱负的演员。这是我的博客。我住在天朝的帝都，有条叫做杰克的狗。&lt;/blockquote&gt;

……公司博客可以这样写：

&lt;blockquote&gt;XYZ Doohickey公司成立于1971年，自从建立以来，我们一直向社会贡献着优秀doohicky。我们的公司总部位于天朝魔都，有着超过两千名员工，对魔都政府税收有着巨大贡献。&lt;/blockquote&gt;

您可以访问&lt;a href=&quot;http://pixwind.com/wp-admin/&quot;&gt;仪表盘&lt;/a&gt;，删除本页面，然后添加您自己的内容。祝您使用愉快！</column>

            <column name="post_content">人们都躲在
所谓理想筑起的堡垒里
只留几个小孔
向外窥望

为了传说中的爱情
我挣脱自己的堡垒
对准了一个目标
发起了一次次冲锋
无奈堡垒太坚固
我退了回来

最后
我用所剩无几的真诚
捆绑了一个结实炸药包
压了上去

一阵硝烟散去
那堡垒
依然坚固
而我
却被炸得粉碎

人们像往常一样
加固着自己的堡垒
我掩埋好上一个我的尸体
在暗夜里
继续
匍匐前行

            <column name="post_content">睡眼惺忪
微凉的清晨
我在宽松的高速路驾车飞奔
傍晚我喜欢追着落日
早晨我喜欢迎着朝阳
道路总没有尽头
短暂停留只是为了更远的行程
车轮总亲吻着路面
无论道路多遥远
所以它们是幸福的

早安
在路上的人们

短暂停留只是为了更远的行程
车轮总亲吻着路面
无论道路多遥远
所以它们是幸福的
早安
在路上的人们

&lt;em&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color: #999999;&quot;&gt;2011.8.21&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/em&gt;</column>

“苍苍九峰北麓，茫茫淀山湖之滨”，朱家角镇位于上海市青浦区中南部，紧靠淀山湖风景区。从市区出发时下着小雨，在人民广场乘车前往朱家角镇，车程一小时，中午时分到达。细雨下会儿停会儿，但并不影响大家游玩的心情。我撑伞边逛边拍，细雨中逛古镇，蛮有味道，只是没有佳人作伴。

&lt;!--more--&gt;

            <column name="post_content">&lt;a href=&quot;http://pixwind.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/chengdu_07.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;alignnone size-full wp-image-112&quot; src=&quot;http://pixwind.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/chengdu_07.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;chengdu_07&quot; width=&quot;480&quot; height=&quot;640&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

来成都出差已半月，成都向来以慢著称，然而工作节奏依然慢不下来，因为本地的客户一点不急，着急的是我们。难得某天出来逛逛，宽窄巷子，锦里，茶楼，美味小吃，精美的手工艺品，还有静静流淌的府南河……只有放慢脚步，才能享受到这个城市特有的柔软时光。&lt;!--more--&gt;

&amp;nbsp;
